US-Mexico Border

Discovery of Remains of Ancient People 58

Soyopa, Mexico, December 12th, Associated Press - The scientific expedition led by Dr. Cummings of the University of Arizona today discovered evidence that people on Earth in prehistoric times were abnormally large. This evidence was discovered 160 miles south of the US-Mexico border, in the area inhabited by the Yaqui tribe. What was discovered was the remains of an infant, whose height was six feet eight inches. Scientists have previously found three skeletons of giants near this location, from which it can be inferred that this place must have been the burial place of ancient giants at that time. In addition, Dr. Cummings also found four sets of children's bones and several jars filled with ash today. Several other exquisitely crafted pottery were also found.

Public Telegram 59

Gansu Relief Committee Telegram to Shanghai Shen Bao:

Since the earthquake in Gansu in the ninth year of the Republic (1920), the province has not recovered. In recent years, disasters have been frequent. Millions of people have died from war, plague, freezing, and famine. This year, in counties such as Gangu, Wushan, Qin'an, Xihe, and Xigu, the wind god has wreaked havoc, and the ears of wheat have withered and died in a few days. In Lintao and Dingxi, hail has caused disaster, and the harvested crops have been almost destroyed in a moment. In Gaolan, Jingyuan, Huining, Yuzhong, and other counties, there was a severe drought in the summer, and the fertile fields cracked like turtle shells. In the autumn, there was a severe frost, and the crops were withered. Yongdeng, Yongjing, Longxi, Dingxi, and the northern border of Huan County were ravaged as if the fields were cut. Swarms of five-colored rats are unprecedented in ancient and modern times. In counties such as Jinta and Shandan, there are both drought and banditry. Refugees are everywhere. In Zhang County, Yanjing, Peijiabao, Wushan, Xiejiaping, Gangu Pan'an Town, Lintao Guanbao, and other places, hundreds of innocent people were killed by bandits in May and June. The damage caused by the loss of other county towns, massacres, looting, etc. is even greater. In famine years, grain prices soar, and the sound of sorrowful cries echoes in the central marshes. Bandits are rampant, and soldiers are fierce. Isolated swallows lose their forest homes. The number of famine victims gathered in the provincial capital is even greater than last year. Various counties are requesting relief one after another. What tactics can be used to deal with this? Only humbly request your newspaper to publicize it on our behalf, so as to appeal to the public so that benevolent assistance and righteous grains can benefit the remnants. We are overwhelmed with urgent gratitude.

Gansu Provincial Relief Committee, respectfully.

Important News (for reprint)

Chairman Chiang Departs Nanchang for Lushan 60

He, Lu, and Other Generals Immediately Return to Defense

Chiang's Overall Response to Petitioning Citizens

Nanchang Correspondence - Chairman Chiang departed from the province for Xun today (the 11th) and then went to Lushan for a day or two of sightseeing before going to Hankou. It is said that Chairman Chiang is eager to return to Nanjing as New Year's Day is approaching. After arriving in Hankou, he may suspend his trip to Hunan. He Jian was summoned to Hankou to be personally instructed on everything. Only Shao Lizi and Zhou Fohai accompanied Chiang to Lushan. Personnel from various offices of the headquarters went directly to Hankou. The details of Chiang's departure for Lushan are recorded as follows:

Grand Occasion of Departure from the Province - Chiang got up very early this morning. Because people from all walks of life did not get prior notice, there were fewer people to see him off. Military and political dignitaries, such as Commanders Lu and Zhu, and Division Commanders Zhang and Gong, all arrived at the Baihuazhou headquarters first to wait. Commissioners from the Provincial Party Department, the Provincial Government, and leaders of various agencies went directly to the Niu Hang Station to wait. This morning, from Zhongshan Road to Yanjiang Road to Niu Hang Station, military and police were densely deployed and security was extremely tight. At half past seven, Chairman Chiang, accompanied by He Chengjun, Shao Lizi, Zhou Fohai, and dozens of staff members from the headquarters, left the headquarters in more than a dozen cars. Lu and others also followed in cars. When they arrived at the Zhangwai River embankment, they fired a 21-gun salute. The welcomers took off their hats and paid their respects. Chiang, He, and others got out of the car at the crossing and boarded a ferry across the river to the Niu Hang Station and boarded the train. Commanders Lu, Zhu, Zhang, and Gong all went to the train to say goodbye to Chiang and He. At about eight o'clock, the welcomers got off the train, and the special train left for Jiujiang amidst military music.

Generals Return to Defense - Chief He and Commander Lu originally planned to accompany Chiang to Lushan for a visit. Later, because of the importance of the military affairs of suppressing the bandits, they did not succeed. After arriving in Xun, He returned to Hankou by warship without delay. Lu also made some deployments in the province and led the Ninth Route Army headquarters to Ji. Division Commanders Zhang and Gong are scheduled to return to their original defenses tomorrow and work hard to clear the area. However, Deng Ying, the commander of the New 13th Division, was dismissed by Chiang for the loss of Ji'an some time ago and handed over to the Ninth Route Army headquarters for discussion. Peng Xueyou, the magistrate of Ji'an County, was also escorted to the province for punishment to appease the people of Ji'an and to serve as a warning. Regarding the position of commander of the New 13th Division, Chiang sent Lu Xiaochen to Fuzhou to take over.

Chairman Chiang's Remarks - Chairman Chiang made the following remarks regarding the petitions of the people of Jiangxi: "I have received many petitions from Jiangxi compatriots during this trip to Gan, and after reviewing them, I have learned about the recent situation in Jiangxi and the hopes of the people. The government should try its best to accommodate the demands of the people within the possible scope, but there are also those that are not permitted by the environment or that the government is currently unable to achieve. The people must also put themselves in the government's position and consider the government's situation, and should not make extravagant demands. Summarizing the petitions from various parties, the important ones are nothing more than the following three points, which are explained separately: (1) I have heard that some people are dissatisfied with the Jiangxi Provincial Government and are criticizing Chairman Lu and Division Commander Zhang. It must be known that the Communist bandits in Gansu are so rampant. The military strength in Gansu is so weak. The area of ​​Gansu is so vast, and Chairman Lu is able to protect most of the important cities in Jiangxi with a very small number of troops. It cannot be said that he is not fulfilling his responsibilities, nor can it be said that he is not responding appropriately. It must be known that the work of suppressing the Communists can only succeed if the officials and the people cooperate effectively. If the people do not fulfill their responsibilities and do not do their best, but only know how to rely on the government and even criticize the individuals in charge of the government, then no matter how hard the government authorities work and how diligently they fulfill their duties, they will not be able to achieve the effect of suppressing the Communists. Therefore, the people of Jiangxi should understand the government's difficult situation and understand the importance of their own qualifications. They should change their passive attitude of relying on the government and criticizing the government, and adopt a positive attitude of assisting the government and working hard on their own. Then, with the joint efforts of officials and people, the Communist bandits will not be difficult to suppress, and the people of Jiangxi can conceive of a happy life of peace and industry. (2) My only task in coming to Gan this time is to suppress the Communists. The disaster situation in Jiangxi, where the Communist bandits have ravaged the land, is extremely serious. The government should provide relief. However, the government's current responsibility is to use its full strength to suppress the Communists, in other words, to use its full strength to liberate the people oppressed by the Communist bandits and to rescue the areas ravaged by the Communist bandits. In order to achieve the goal of suppressing the Communists, it is not enough to raise military expenses. At this time of financial hardship, the government cannot raise a large amount of relief funds in addition to military salaries, nor can it transfer military expenses for relief funds. Although the State Council previously approved 8 million yuan in relief funds for Shaanxi, it has not been possible to raise funds to this day due to the government's inability to do so. Mr. Yu Youren's trip to Shaanxi only brought more than 100,000 yuan in relief funds. However, the government will never ignore the disaster situation in Gansu. I will normally allocate 100,000 yuan from the military expenses I brought to Gan for relief efforts in Jiangxi. I know that this is a drop in the bucket and will not help much, but it is only to express the government's concern for the disaster in Gan. The people of Jiangxi should understand that the current priority is to actively raise military expenses and suppress the Communists, and not to start from the negative side. I sincerely hope that people with resources and wealth in various places will come forward to take responsibility, contribute their wealth and do their best to assist the government, and use the power of society to carry out large-scale relief donations. Then, by gathering small things to make big things, and accumulating earth to make mountains, it is not entirely impossible, depending on the efforts of the compatriots. (3) It is a matter of course that education funds should be independent. However, Jiangxi currently has a special situation. The Communist bandits are rampant, and alerts are being issued everywhere. Local income is mostly cut off, and the provincial government's income has decreased while expenditures remain the same. Therefore, the arrears of education funds are an inevitable phenomenon in fact. My colleagues in the education sector are all intellectuals and should know that in the current period of suppressing the Communists, my farmers, industrialists, merchants, students, and soldiers should all endure temporary suffering. The entire body is mobilized to use its full strength to suppress the Communists. All construction projects must wait until the Communists are suppressed before there can be development. If my colleagues in the education sector express dissatisfaction due to short-term arrears of wages, then how will the officers and soldiers who give their lives and throw their heads to suppress the Communists, who are still inevitably owed wages, fare? My colleagues in the education sector should know that the responsibility of suppressing the Communists is by no means lighter for the education sector than for the military. Since the military is suffering in the front, how can my education sector bear to be alone? Once the Communists are suppressed and society is stable, the local finances will be unified, income will increase, and education funds will not be lacking. Therefore, the independence of Jiangxi's education funds should be maintained and the original plan should be guaranteed. However, in the event that there are temporary difficulties in practice during the period of suppressing the Communists, it is also hoped that my colleagues in the education sector will endure temporary suffering and understand the government's environment. I have come to Gan this time with a twelve-point determination and effort to suppress the Communists to save my people in Jiangxi. This is enough to comfort my compatriots. However, the people of Jiangxi should also assist the government and assist the army with a twelve-point determination and effort to achieve the complete success of suppressing the Communists. It is best not to be disappointed or resentful with the government because of the transitional period, where the government may not be able to fully satisfy people's wishes." (December 11)

Lu Xiaochen Replaces Commander of the New 13th Division 61

Deng Ying Is Dismissed and Punished for Ineffective Bandit Suppression

Nanchang Correspondence - After Deng Ying, the commander of the New 13th Division, was transferred from Hubei to Gan, he was stationed near Ji'an, and he built strong trenches and electric fences, which could be firmly defended. However, on October 2, when Zhu Mao advanced into Ji'an from Lianhua and Yongxin, Deng did not fire a shot and retreated, causing Ji'an to be easily obtained by the bandits. The essence of more than a dozen counties in western Gan has been wiped out. After investigation, it was confirmed that the Communist bandits killed more than 10,000 people in Ji'an and burned and destroyed houses, causing losses of property that are difficult to calculate. Moreover, after the loss of Ji'an, Deng's division was stationed in Fuzhou, and the loss of Yihuang and Le'an was like watching a fire from across the river and not moving. Nearly two regiments of the division stationed in Chongren, with several Communist bandits' handguns, also entered the city safely, and the officers and soldiers did not resist at all. In early November, when Zhu Mao planned to attack Fuzhou from Chongyi, Deng Ying wanted to abandon Fuzhou again without thinking about blocking the attack, causing the Communist bandits to advance to more than twenty miles from the county town of Linchuan, near Dundu and Liufang. Fortunately, Wang Zhenhuan, the county magistrate of the county, maintained his composure and supervised the Zhou team leader to defend firmly, so it did not waver. Unexpectedly, Deng Ying declared to Magistrate Wang that he would not fight the bandits without 50,000 yuan. After getting the money, he demolished dozens of shops in Linchuan Wenchang Bridge and Hedong Bay. All these perverse acts are difficult to record. After Chairman Chiang arrived in Gan, the people of Ji'an complained to Chiang about Deng's various illegal acts. The important points are: (1) When in Ji, residents in the county had to obtain a pass from the division headquarters, each costing one yuan or one thousand cash. Deng also borrowed rent from the business community for several months and extorted donations, and the income from the search was no less than 100,000 yuan. (2) If there was a young girl in a civilian family, Deng would always ask her for pleasure. If he did not succeed, he would falsely accuse her of being a Communist bandit and arrest her and imprison her. There were also those who could not bear his oppression and allowed him to destroy them. (3) When the Communist bandits advanced to more than ten miles from the city of Ji, Deng was still patting his chest to the representatives of all walks of life and was responsible for keeping the city. The words were still in his ears, but the entire army fled in the dark night, causing more than 100,000 people in the city of Ji to not know where to die. (4) He indulged his soldiers in disturbing the residents. For example, when he was in Fu, he cut open more than a dozen suitcases of a resident named Jiang in the name of inspection and looted his valuables. (5) Deng's troops were extremely undisciplined. For example, when he was in Fu, there were those who openly raped women, and Deng ignored it. (6) Deng brought three or four concubines with him when he supervised the division in Fu. The rest are difficult to describe. After Chiang obtained dozens of petitions and reports from various parties, he was shocked and immediately summoned Deng to the province. When Deng arrived in the province from Fu on the evening of the 9th and met General Commander Chiang, Chiang immediately dismissed Deng from his position and ordered him to be arrested and handed over to the Ninth Route Army Command for custody to await strict legal punishment. In addition, Peng Xueyou, the magistrate of Ji'an County, has also been escorted to the province to be punished for the crime of dereliction of duty and harming the people. After Chiang dismissed Deng, he appointed Lu Xiaochen, the current member of the Gan Provincial Government and senior advisor to the Ninth Route Army, as the commander of the New 13th Division.

The Third Division is mostly the old department of various routes. After Lu was appointed, he rushed to Fuzhou on the morning of the 13th after sending Chiang to Xun, leading the security team, guards, and many attendants to take over the affairs. There are divisions of Mao Bingwen, Tan Daoyuan, etc. in Fuzhou, which can be safely received. In addition, after Chiang dismissed Deng, he telegraphed to the commanders of various routes to show military discipline and to warn them. The original telegram reads:

"He, Deputy Director of the Headquarters, Commander He, General Commander Chiang, Commander Lu, Commander Zhu, Xunjian, Deng Ying, the commander of the New 13th Division, was cowardly and did not move forward in suppressing the bandits in western Gansu. He abandoned Ji'an without orders, causing the Communist bandits to kill and slaughter the people, who were in dire straits. If he is not severely punished according to law, it is not enough to promote law and order and thank the people. In addition to being dismissed from his position and arrested for strict legal punishment, he should also order his subordinates to know the importance of being one." (December 12)

He Jian Arrives in Hankou 62

Hankou Dispatch: He Jian, the General Commander of the Fourth Route Army and concurrently Chairman of the Hunan Provincial Government, arrived in Hubei on the afternoon of the 11th at 2:00 PM via special express train from Hunan, as General Commander Chiang was soon to arrive in Hankou. He arrived at the Gu Yu Tao train station in Wuchang at 10:00 AM on the 12th. Accompanying him were Huang Weihan, the Chief of Staff of the Fourth Route Army; Ling Daru, the Secretary; Hu Yinhuai, the Director of Public Relations; and He Zuan, Yang Xunqin, and over ten other representatives from the Hunan Province Compatriot Women's Disaster Relief Fundraising Group. Waiting at the station to welcome him were Xia Douyin, Liu Wendao, and others. After alighting from the train, He Jian crossed the river and resided at the Fourth Route Army's office in Hankou. I ventured to visit him and inquired about the recent situation regarding the suppression of bandits. He Jian stated that Hunan Province had suffered the most from banditry. However, after vigorous suppression by various armies, the main force of the bandits had been defeated, leaving only scattered small groups. Recently, in the Pingjiang area, Kong Hechong's bandit units had been successively attacked by the troops led by Liu Jianxu, the Army Commander, and under the command of Wang Dongyuan and Tao Guang, with victories achieved in Jia Yi and Changshou. The bandits had built strong fortifications near Changshou, which our army broke through after several days and nights of bloody hand-to-hand combat. Furthermore, continuous bombing by the air force resulted in the death of over a thousand bandits, with countless wounded. The remaining bandits are now fleeing towards Tonggu and Xiushui in western Jiangxi. Our army is continuing to pursue and attack them, while Jiangxi Province troops are blocking key areas to ensure a quick resolution. In the Liuyang area, since the recovery by Chen Guangzhong's division, they are now searching and suppressing areas near Lianhu and Dongmen City. Army Commander Liu Jianxu also plans to implement concrete post-disaster measures step by step. At the same time, given that Pingjiang and Liuyang counties are connected to Xiushui and Wanzai in Jiangxi Province, and Chongyang and Tongshan in Hubei Province, and are intertwined with Changli and Baxiang, with overlapping mountain ranges, making suppression difficult, I plan to select a suitable central location to convene a joint defense conference to coordinate efforts and achieve a combined attack. In western Hunan, since Commander Li Xue led his troops, together with Zhang Ying's Sichuan army and Dai Huiyuan, Chen Quzhen, and other units, to encircle the area, the bandit He originally intended to flee back to Changtao, but our army, with its soldiers giving their all, launched a surprise attack from Changtao overnight. The bandits then fled from Shimen and Linli towards Jinshi and Fengzhou. Fortunately, our army's swift pursuit led to the successive recovery of Shimen and Linli, and the simultaneous relief of Jinshi and Fengzhou. With no way to advance or retreat, the bandits fled to Zhangjia Factory and Wangjia Factory. We are currently combining efforts with various armies to launch a joint attack, and it will not be difficult to wipe them out in one fell swoop. In addition, in the Huarong area, because Zhang Ying's Sichuan army was transferred to defend the border of Hubei Province and Jianli, the remaining bandits took advantage of the opportunity to infiltrate. Chen Cheng's division and detachments from Li Jue's and Zhang Ying's divisions, along with Liu Peixu's brigade, have surrounded the city from all sides, and the city has been reported to be recovered. This time, I came to Hankou specifically to welcome the Commander-in-Chief to Hunan to oversee the suppression of the remaining bandits, so that the fundamental elimination of the bandit communists and the early realization of political tutelage and construction can be achieved.

Important News II

National Seal Jade Material Transported from Tianjin to Beijing 63

The New Provincial Government Dispatches Guanglu to Escort the Material

Tianjin Dispatch: Hetian jade from Xinjiang Province is renowned throughout the world. The imperial seals used by the Qing Dynasty were all sourced from this area. When Yuan Shikai declared himself emperor, the seals he planned to create were also sourced from Hetian. Last year, the National Government planned to create a jade seal and specifically ordered the Xinjiang Provincial Government to send someone to select and deliver the material to Beijing for use. Currently, the jade material has been selected by the New Provincial Government, which has specially dispatched Guanglu, an advisor to the Provincial Government and the current Consul in Zaisang, Soviet Union, to escort the material. Guanglu brought the jade stone via the Siberian Railway through Dong Province and arrived in Tianjin yesterday. He represented Jin Shuren, the Chairman of the province, to meet with Vice Commander Zhang Xueliang to convey his greetings. He will soon depart for Nanjing to present the jade to the National Government. I visited Guanglu at his hotel yesterday, and he showed me the jade, which was tightly wrapped and highly valued. It is irregularly triangular in shape and weighs over thirty catties. One side is yellowish-red, like the seal stones produced in Changhua, while the other side is light ink in color. The bottom reveals white. The entire stone is crystal clear, lustrous, and radiant. A corner reveals several inches of jade, as white and smooth as fat. From this rough stone, one can already see the preciousness it contains. According to Guanglu, the jade was produced in a river in Hetian. An experienced jade worker was able to identify the aura on the water's surface and determine the location of the jade. However, small pieces are easy to find, while large pieces are quite difficult to obtain. The New Provincial Government ordered the Hetian Dao to be responsible for the extraction and construction, which took years to complete. Two pieces were finally obtained. One piece is being transported by camel through the grasslands into the customs, but has not yet arrived. The jade quality is slightly inferior, but it will be used as a backup selection. The jade quality of this piece is extremely fine. After carving, it can yield a huge piece of eight inches square and is entirely clear and free of impurities and patterns. It is truly the highest grade of mutton-fat jade and is suitable for use by the state. Guanglu also elaborated on the various construction projects undertaken in Xinjiang Province in recent years, stating that since Chairman Jin Shuren took office, he has actively developed various undertakings. Most of the province's financial revenue is used for construction, while administrative expenses are kept to a minimum. The province has newly built many automobile roads that extend in all directions, all starting from the provincial capital, Dihua. These include the Digu, Dita, Diyi, Diha, and Dia lines. Digu runs from Dihua to Guchengzi in the east, and Dita runs from Dihua to Tacheng in the northwest, bordering Russia. Both have been opened to traffic. Diyi to Yili, Diha to Haxhi, and Dia to Altay are all under construction and are expected to be open to traffic next year. A provincial road bureau has been established in the provincial capital specifically for this purpose. There are currently over two hundred automobiles traveling back and forth, transporting passengers and goods. The biggest plan at present is to build the Xin-Sui automobile road, which runs from Xinjiang to Suiyuan and connects to the Ping-Sui Railway to transport Northwest local products for sale in the interior. Chairman Jin has been considering this plan for a long time, but it has not been implemented because the route is too long and difficult to survey. A Northwest Scientific Expedition Team that departed from Pingliang by automobile thirteen days ago traveled through Suiyuan to Xinjiang. Upon receiving the team's report, Jin decided to proceed and has sent two automobiles to survey the proposed route to Guihua City, the provincial capital of Suiyuan. He also sent me to Tianjin and Shanghai to order a number of automobiles from foreign merchants for use when the road is opened to traffic. He also plans to contact foreign merchants in Tianjin to order aircraft for communication with the interior and for the transportation of passengers and goods. The postal and telecommunications services in Xinjiang are poorly managed. The provincial government has built a long-wave radio station in Dihua and established a radio school to train radio personnel. I have also been ordered to order several short-wave radio materials to be installed in key areas within the country and the province for communication purposes. The provincial government also operates several yarn factories and ranches, all of which have achieved good results. The self-woven fabrics are now able to compete with foreign goods, and the number of Russian fabrics has gradually decreased. The ranches are researching and improving horse and sheep breeds. Several purebred horses and curly-haired sheep have been purchased from Russia and distributed to the Yili, Dihua, and Barke ranches for improving the breeds of sheep and horses. Purebred horses are the best in the world, and curly-haired sheep produce better wool than western sheep. This type of undertaking is best suited for Xinjiang Province. (December 10th)

Development of Shandong Long-Distance Telephone Service 64

Jinan Dispatch: Since the establishment of the Long-Distance Telephone Administration by the Department of Construction, the development of long-distance telephone service in this province has been rapidly progressing. To date, service has been opened to more than twenty counties, with operations beginning in over ten counties. Currently, various counties are still actively installing lines. According to Du Desan, the current director of the Administration, the long-distance telephone service in this province was first initiated by Kong Fanhao, the former Director of the Department of Construction, during Chairman Chen (Diaoyuan)'s term. A long-distance telephone training class was established to recruit and teach students in preparation for the installation of lines. By the end of February of this year, a total of 113 students had graduated. Subsequently, when Kong resigned, Chen Luanshu succeeded him as Director of the Department of Construction, but discussions to repair the Lihuo automobile road telephone failed. Until the end of March of this year, the Provincial Government received a telegram from the Central Government ordering the rapid installation of long-distance telephones in the defense area of Ma Hongkui, the General Commander of the 15th Route Army. Consequently, they set out on March 30th and by April 8th, they had installed lines in the five counties of Tai'an, Feicheng, Pingyin, Dong'a, and Dongping. Later, as Chen's former troops were transferred to the Caozhou and Jining areas, the Provincial Government, for the convenience of military affairs, ordered the continued construction of lines in the Cao-Ji area. Thus, they set out on April 17th and by the end of June, they had completed projects in the ten counties of Ruzhang, Ningyang, Jining, Jiaxiang, Juye, Heze, Yuncheng, Jinxiang, Shanxian, and Chengwu. Furthermore, under the order of General Commander Han, they installed a section of line from Zaoyuansi to Qingcheng, and also borrowed telegraph poles to install a section of line from Jinan to Changqing. Later, due to the outbreak of war, the above-mentioned sections of lines were almost completely destroyed. After the recovery of the provincial capital, the Administration dispatched personnel in early September to accompany the transportation battalion of the General Command to install a section of line from Zhoucun to Putai. However, prior to October of this year, the long-distance telephone service in this province was almost completely destroyed, with only one or two sections in operation, failing to form a unified network. In September, I was appointed by the Department of Construction as the concurrently Director of the Long-Distance Telephone Administration and began preparations on the 26th of that month to connect the northeast and southwest lines. On the one hand, I surveyed the condition of the four sections of lines: Ji-Zhang (Jinan-Zhangqiu), Chang-Ping (Changqing-Pingyin), Qing-Xin (Jinan-Xinzhuang), and Zao-Qi (Zaoyuansi-Qidong). On the other hand, I separately prepared budget estimates for the four sections of lines and submitted them to the Department of Construction on October 2nd, requesting that they be submitted to the Provincial Government for discussion. However, due to the delay in receiving funds, the work was delayed until November 9th when the regular expenses for October were finally received. Only then were the four sections of lines expedited, with staff dispatched to start construction and soldiers requested from the transportation battalion of the General Command to assist. The Ji-Xin section, which was fifteen li long, was completed on November 11th. The Ji-Zhang section, which was one hundred and ten li long, was completed on November 23rd. The Chang-Ping section, which was one hundred li long, was completed on November 24th. The Zao-Qi section, which was ninety-five li long, was also completed by the end of November. However, the Ji-Chang section, because it was borrowed from telegraph poles, the Telegraph Bureau has not yet received an order from the Ministry of Transportation, and the poles have not been continuously lent, leading to the route being cut off and requiring a new plan. Although the Zhoucun-Putai line is open, it has not been connected to Jinan. Therefore, it was proposed to the Provincial Government for discussion to continue repairing a section of line between Zhangqiu and Changshan, which has been approved by the Provincial Government and is being prepared for construction. The list of counties connected by each section of line and those currently under construction is listed below: (1) Cao-Ji Area: Jining, Jiaxiang, Juye, Dancheng, Jinxiang, Yutai, Shanxian, and Wucheng have been connected and began operations at the end of November. (2) Tai'an, Feicheng, Pingyin, Changqing, and Dong'a counties. (3) Zaoyuansi, Zhangqiu, Qidong, and Qingcheng counties. (4) Jining to Wenshang: The above three lines have been connected but have not yet begun operations. (5) Between Ningyang, Wenshang, Dongping, and Dong'a. (6) Between Juye and Heze: The above two lines were originally open, but were heavily damaged due to military events this summer and have not yet been repaired. (7) Between Jinan and Changqing. (8) Between Zhangqiu and Changshan: The above two lines are currently under construction. (9) Zhoucun, Changshan, Huantai, Gaoyuan, Boxing, and Putai: Although there are poles and lines, branch offices have not yet been established for organization. (10) Between Jinan and Zhangqiu: Service began on the 1st of this month.

Tianjin-Pukou Railway to Improve 1st and 2nd Class Passenger Trains 67

Three Cars Added for Military Personnel on Official Duty

Since the outbreak of the war, many vehicles on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway have been lost. Of all the passenger trains in operation, only the Ping-Pu train and the Beijing-Liaoning through train are able to operate on time and regularly, and the vehicles are also in good order. The remaining special express trains, such as the 1st and 2nd class trains, are assembled from various sources and are often occupied by military personnel. Although the director of the railway has tried his best to rectify the situation, it is impossible to do so until the end of the war. Now that the war has ended, the number of wounded soldiers and military personnel traveling back and forth on official duty has not decreased, and travelers who buy tickets have no place to stand. In order to protect the passengers, Director Sun of the railway has strictly ordered the Traffic Department to add three cars for military personnel on official duty to the 1st and 2nd class trains. In the future, military personnel will not be allowed to sit in passenger cars. He has also strictly ordered the police sections along the line to cooperate with the military police accompanying the trains to effectively crack down on violations. It is said that this will be implemented starting today. China National Aviation Corporation.

Chongqing Plane Lands in Zhenjiang 68

Both Pilots and Two Passengers Are Safe

Yesterday (12th) at 1:00 PM, the China National Aviation Corporation's Chongqing plane, flying from Hankou to Shanghai, experienced a carburetor malfunction over Longtan, and gasoline leaked out. It then landed on the riverbank. A British warship passing by saw the plane drifting on the river and stopped to inquire, then turned around and towed the plane back to the town. It passed the Zhenjiang customs patrol boat Zhenping on the 12th, who took over the towing to Zhenjiang. It was already 3:00 PM. The plane was docked behind another British warship stationed in Zhenjiang. Upon hearing the news, I went to inspect the plane. It was a biplane amphibious aircraft. The two wings and rudder were yellow, and the fuselage was dark gray-black. The cockpit could accommodate two people, and the passenger cabin behind could accommodate six. The words "Chongqing" were written on the back of the plane, with an eagle symbol in front of the words. The plane door was tightly closed, and no one was visible. I also went to the post office to investigate and learned that the mail carried by the plane had been transferred to the Beijing-Shanghai special express train to Shanghai. At 10:00 PM, I learned that the Chinese pilot, Mr. Zhou Junhuang, was staying at the Dahua Hotel, so I went to visit him and had a brief conversation with him: (Question) Where did the plane land? (Answer) Near Longtan. (Question) Did you encounter wind? (Answer) No, there was damage to the engine. (Question) Where was the damage? (Answer) The carburetor tube screw was broken, causing gasoline to leak. (Question) Were the engine parts still running when you landed? (Answer) Yes. (Question) Why not fix it immediately? (Answer) It cannot be repaired in a short time. (Question) How did you get to Zhenjiang safely? (Answer) A British warship, Sarphdo4, was passing by and we asked them to tow us to Zhenjiang. At the 12th fort, we met the Zhenjiang customs patrol boat Zhenping, who brought us safely to Zhenjiang. (Question) Who was flying the plane with you? (Answer) An American, Vaughn. (Question) Where is Mr. Buddha now? (Answer) On the British warship. (This ship is stationed in Zhenjiang). (Question) How many passengers were on board? (Answer) A Chinese man boarded in Hankou, and a Westerner boarded in Nanjing. They have now been sent ashore to take the train to Shanghai. (Question) When will you return to Shanghai? (Answer) We will fly back to Shanghai after the parts arrive in the town and are repaired. (Question) Where did you graduate? (Answer) United States. (Question) How many planes does the airline have? (Answer) Six. Two have already been damaged.

Full Text of Civil Code Inheritance Section 69

The two sections of the Civil Code concerning relatives and inheritance have previously been passed by the Legislative Yuan in the third reading and submitted to the National Government for promulgation. Yesterday (12th), the second meeting of the National Government resolved to promulgate them. The full text of the Inheritance Section is recorded below: Chapter I Heirs to the Estate (Article 1138) The heirs to the estate, excluding the spouse, shall be determined according to the following order: 1. Lineal descendants by blood; 2. Parents; 3. Siblings; 4. Grandparents. (Article 1139) Among the heirs in the first order specified in the preceding article, those of closer degrees of kinship shall have priority. (Article 1140) If any of the heirs in the first order specified in Article 1138 dies or loses the right of inheritance before the commencement of the inheritance, their lineal descendants by blood shall inherit their portion by representation. (Article 1141) When there are several heirs of the same order, they shall inherit equally according to the number of persons, unless otherwise provided by law. (Article 1142) The order of inheritance of adopted children shall be the same as that of children born in wedlock. The share of inheritance of adopted children shall be one-half of that of children born in wedlock, but if the adoptive parents have no lineal descendants by blood as heirs, their share of inheritance shall be the same as that of children born in wedlock. (Article 1143) If there are no lineal descendants by blood, a will may be made to designate an heir for all or part of the property, but this shall not violate the provisions concerning compulsory portions. (Article 1144) Spouses have the right to inherit each other's estate. Their share of inheritance shall be determined according to the following provisions: 1. When inheriting together with the heirs of the first order specified in Article 1138, their share of inheritance shall be equal to that of other heirs on average; 2. When inheriting together with the heirs of the second or third order specified in Article 1138, their share of inheritance shall be one-half of the estate; 3. When inheriting together with the heirs of the fourth order specified in Article 1138, their share of inheritance shall be two-thirds of the estate; 4. If there are no heirs of the first to fourth orders specified in Article 1138, their share of inheritance shall be the entire estate. (Article 1145) Any person with any of the following circumstances shall lose their right of inheritance: 1. Intentionally causing the death of the deceased or an heir, or being sentenced to imprisonment for causing their death; 2. Using fraud or coercion to induce the deceased to make a will regarding inheritance, or to revoke or alter it; 3. Using fraud or coercion to obstruct the deceased from making a will regarding inheritance, or to obstruct its revocation or alteration; 4. Forging, altering, concealing, or destroying a will of the deceased regarding inheritance; 5. Committing serious abuse or insult against the deceased, and the deceased has expressed that they may not inherit. The provisions of paragraphs 2 to 4 of the preceding paragraph shall not apply if the deceased has forgiven the act, and their right of inheritance shall not be lost. (Article 1146) If the right of inheritance is infringed, the injured party or their legal representative may request its restoration. The right to request restoration shall be extinguished if it is not exercised within two years from the time of knowing of the infringement, or after ten years from the commencement of the inheritance. Chapter II Inheritance of the Estate Section 1 Effects (Article 1147) Inheritance begins upon the death of the deceased. (Article 1148) From the commencement of the inheritance, the heir shall succeed to all the rights and obligations of the deceased in respect of property, except as otherwise provided in this Law. However, rights and obligations that are exclusively personal to the deceased shall not be included. (Article 1149) Persons who have been continuously supported by the deceased during their lifetime shall be given a share of the estate by the relatives' conference according to the degree of support they have received and other relationships. (Article 1150) The costs of estate management, division, and execution of the will shall be paid from the estate, unless they are incurred due to the negligence of the heir. (Article 1151) When there are several heirs, they shall have common ownership of the entire estate before it is divided. (Article 1152) The jointly owned estate mentioned in the preceding article may be managed by one person elected by the heirs. (Article 1153) The heirs shall be jointly and severally liable for the debts of the deceased. The heirs shall bear the debts of the deceased in proportion to their respective shares of inheritance, unless otherwise agreed. Section 2 Limited Inheritance (Article 1154) The heirs may limit their liability for the debts of the deceased to the extent of the estate they have inherited. When one of the heirs claims limited inheritance as mentioned in the preceding paragraph, the other heirs shall be deemed to have also limited their inheritance. Heirs with limited inheritance shall not have their rights and obligations towards the deceased extinguished by the inheritance. (Article 1155) Heirs with limited inheritance under the preceding article shall be subject to the provisions of Articles 1156 to 1163. (Article 1156) Heirs with limited inheritance shall prepare and submit an inventory of the estate to the court within three months from the commencement of the inheritance. The court may extend the three-month deadline if deemed necessary based on the heir's request. (Article 1157) When the heir submits the report to the court as stipulated in the preceding article, the court shall issue a public notice requiring the creditors of the deceased to declare their claims within a specified period. The specified period shall not be less than three months. (Article 1158) Within the specified period stipulated in the preceding article, the heir shall not repay any debt to any creditor of the deceased. (Article 1159) After the expiration of the specified period stipulated in Article 1157, the heir shall pay the debts declared within the specified period and the debts known to the heir in proportion to their respective amounts with the estate, but this shall not prejudice the interests of persons with priority rights. (Article 1160) The heir may not deliver the bequest to the legatee until the debts have been repaid in accordance with the provisions of the preceding article. (Article 1161) If the heir violates the provisions of Articles 1157 to 1160 and causes damage to the creditors of the deceased, they shall be liable for compensation. The injured party may request the creditor or legatee who has unduly received payment to return the amount they have unduly received. (Article 1162) Creditors of the deceased who do not declare their claims within the specified period stipulated in Article 1157 and are unknown to the heir may only exercise their rights against the remaining estate. (Article 1163) Heirs who have any of the following circumstances may not claim the benefits stipulated in Article 1154: 1. Concealing the estate; 2. Making false entries in the inventory of the estate; 3. Disposing of the estate with the intention of defrauding the rights of the creditors of the deceased. (To be continued)

Wuhu Urgent News 70

The Wuhu General Chamber of Commerce, regarding year-end accounting matters, specially convened an emergency meeting at 2:00 PM today. A resolution was made to telegraph the Anhui Provincial Government, stating that the Provincial Education Department had already approved the extension of the winter vacation for schools in the province, continuing from January 26th for four weeks. It would be extremely difficult for the business community to complete year-end accounting within a limited time frame. Investigations revealed that wholesale stores in Wuhu had extended credit to the hinterland totaling seven or eight million yuan. It is impossible to collect all debts by year-end, which will inevitably lead to major disputes and business decline in the coming year. Various industries will inevitably face innocent bankruptcy. It is earnestly requested that adjustments be made to alleviate this dire situation.

Bao Geng, the outgoing special commissioner of finance for Anhui, was previously arrested and detained by the Wuhu Municipal Public Security Bureau under the orders of Chen Tiaoyuan, and later escorted to Anqing. According to provincial sources, the provincial government has received a telegram from Beijing and has restored Bao's freedom, allowing him to remain in Anqing to handle the handover.

The Wuhu Municipal Public Security Bureau convened a winter defense meeting at 4:00 PM today, deciding that military police, merchants, and community organizations will be responsible for different areas. Strict inspections of travelers and shantytowns will be implemented starting today.

The former Fifth and Twenty-Sixth Rear Hospitals in Wuhu had personnel sent by the General Headquarters' Wounded Soldier Clearing Office to handle the closure. The Twenty-Sixth Rear Hospital officially announced its closure yesterday. All wounded soldiers were transported to Beijing that night. The Fifth Hospital will also be closed down within days.

The headquarters of the 171st Brigade of the 57th Division has been ordered to move to Wuhu. Brigade Commander Wang Leshan has already led his troops from Anqing and is expected to arrive in Wuhu tomorrow. After arriving in Wuhu, Wang will organize a separate military police investigation office responsible for maintaining security in Wuhu (11th). Local correspondence

Qingpu 71

A large group of refugees expelled from the territory. Yesterday, a large group of refugees from Henan passed through the county. Songjiang 73

Inspector Yang captures kidnappers. Yang Shijie, an inspector from the Public Security Bureau, captured Meng Zhongping, Fan A-Liu, Lu Jintu, and three other kidnappers who kidnapped Mr. Shen from Qitangtou, Qingpu, and a young boy surnamed Mou from Xinzhen North. They are now sentenced to detention pending a consultation from the Qingpu County Government to handle the case according to the law.

The front pavilion of the county is not allowed to be reduced. The county government demolished the screen wall in front of the county government to rebuild the high bridge in front of the county government. The county government meeting decided to build a pavilion on the original site of the screen wall and handed it over to the construction bureau for design and construction by a district office. Now that the project has been completed, it was set up a few days ago. However, because the style of the pavilion is tall and large, pedestrians and vehicles in the street must detour. Local people think that the pavilions have never been so tall and that they are very lacking in elegance in the middle of the street. Moreover, it is rare to see such a tall building outside Shanghai Road. The Second District Fire Brigade also sent a letter to request that the scope be reduced and rebuilt, because it would hinder the operation of the fire engine and is related to fire protection. The people also sent a letter to the county requesting that it be changed to a smaller size. The county government held the eighty-seventh county government meeting yesterday to discuss the submission. The meeting decided that the construction pavilion in front of the county government had been discussed and decided three times by this meeting and ordered the first district office to follow suit. At present, it is planned to order the district to fill the sides of the Aiming Bridge to the north immediately, and the utility poles will also be moved to the front of the government. It is also ordered that the Public Security Bureau order the relocation so that it does not hinder fire protection and traffic. The county government's record letter will be sent to the Second District Fire Brigade for reference, so this tall pavilion will probably remain in the middle of the road forever and cannot be changed.

The Education Bureau seeks to offset overdue fines. After the county Education Bureau reported the overdue fines to the province, the Education Bureau planned to offset the funds with any relevant money so as to expand the sources of income. It had already proposed collecting donations for flowers and rice throughout the county, new business tax surcharges, and registration fee surcharges, and submitted them to the county government meeting for discussion. It is heard that the discussion result was that the matter concerned small taxes and the decision was made to first hand it over to the Finance Bureau for review before proceeding. The district police rice subsidy will still be maintained. The salaries and allowances of the district chiefs and police officers in this county are not high. When the summer and autumn rice prices are high, life is even more difficult. They have requested an increase in salary. The county government meeting discussed the matter, thinking that the request was indeed true and that the rice subsidy should be appropriately increased and implemented. Now, the twelfth district office has reported that the rice price has dropped and requested that the rice subsidy for the first branch bureau chief be cancelled. However, it is heard that the county government believes that the rice subsidy for the district chiefs and police officers is only 8.5 yuan per month for each first, second, and third class police officer. At a time when the level of living is increasing day by day, the rice subsidy is a general matter and should not be cancelled. The district is ordered to follow the previous order.

Suzhou 74

Crackdown on refugees staying within the borders. Magistrate Huang previously drafted crackdown measures because refugees often stayed within the borders of the four prefectures of Jiangnan, Suzhou, Songjiang, Changzhou, and Taicang, harming the towns. Subsequently, whenever refugees arrived, the town chiefs, etc., would report to the district office, which would work with the water and land police to escort them back to their hometowns. If resistance or robbery occurred, the ringleaders would be detained and dealt with according to the law. The same measures were forwarded to the counties of Songjiang, Changzhou, and Taicang for implementation, and a request was submitted to the Department of Civil Affairs for approval. The Department of Civil Affairs approved it yesterday (the 13th) and ordered a reply to be faithfully implemented in conjunction with the water and land police.

The National Goods Exhibition will be postponed. The Suzhou National Goods Relief Association and the Shanghai National Goods Maintenance Association jointly launched a mobile exhibition of national goods in Suzhou. It was originally scheduled to be held in December. The General Chamber of Commerce had repeatedly invited both parties to discuss the implementation. However, due to obstacles in the tax-free transportation bill of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, it is heard that it will be postponed to February or March of next year.

Gang bandits linger in Damiao Port, Wujiang. He specially submitted a request to County Magistrate Wu of Wu County yesterday to forward a letter to the Third District of the Water Public Security to immediately order its subordinates to assist in suppressing the bandits. Upon receiving the letter, District Chief Shen immediately ordered Captain Xu of the Fourteenth Team and Captain Fang of the Guerrilla Team to go to various roads to assist in the suppression.

The Water Police Squad Leader is being held under surveillance. The First Squad, Eleventh Team of the Third District of the Water Public Security, stationed in Huangdai Town, arrested a petty thief named Zeng A-Lin in the town and escorted him for legal proceedings. However, due to negligent surveillance, Zeng took the opportunity to escape. Subsequently, the local court believed that the criminal was a habitual thief and had been sentenced to imprisonment. He had been released not long ago and was now committing theft again. It was necessary to file a case for investigation and immediately inform Shen, the district chief of the Third District of the Water Public Security. Shen approved the letter, stating that Zeng's escape was clearly due to the negligence of Yu Hong-Xun, the squad leader. He ordered Pei Xuan, the captain of the Eleventh Ma Team, to first place the squad leader under surveillance. Once the fugitive Zeng was captured, he would issue further instructions. Yesterday (the 13th), Huang, the district chief of Huangdai Town, Gu Kun, and local gentry Qian Jieyi, etc., specially submitted a request to the Third District of the Water Public Security, requesting that the squad be released to ensure local governance. It is not known whether the request will be approved.

The Director of the Construction Engineering Office is replaced. Tang Ying, the Director of the Construction Engineering Office of Jiangsu Province, has had little success since taking office. The business registration fee will be temporarily postponed. The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance stated that the province previously planned to collect business tax registration fees for the police due to the police. The regulations and forms have been issued and the collection director has been dispatched to various counties to investigate and open the office. Now, the Fourth Plenary Session decided to implement the abolition of the tax in January of the 20th year. Since the central government has determined and announced the date of tax abolition, the province's original plan to prepare for the business tax should be changed accordingly. Therefore, a proposal was drafted to postpone the collection of the original business registration fee. The county bureaus were ordered to supervise the directors to comply with the aforementioned forms and actively investigate, register, and create a register, and visit and record the points that should be noted below: (1) In the investigation of the commercial declaration form, the annual business volume and monthly rent of each business household and the number of employees should be added for reference. (2) After the declaration form is filled out by each business and sent to the county bureau, the county bureau will send personnel to review it to avoid omissions. The exact amount should be checked especially for the capital amount. (3) All businesses that should be investigated will only be charged a registration certificate fee of two yuan, and all other fees will be postponed. (4) The magnetic card should be made slowly, if it has been made, it will be retained for changing the business tax. All commercial towns and villages will be investigated and registered. When the central government implements the tax abolition, they will start to change the business tax. The business regulations will be announced separately after being submitted for approval.

Letter from Mao Mu-Jun 83

Sir, in the local section of your newspaper on the 9th of this month, there was a news item about a water police officer shooting a opium robbery case. It stated that Yang Bingsheng, an officer of our district, reported to the High Court that Zhu Youlin had robbed opium worth 36 yuan and embezzled tens of thousands of yuan, and that Chief Mao had released him in exchange for 10,000 yuan. This is completely inconsistent with the facts. It was heard in late June of this year that someone wearing a water police uniform had robbed a large amount of opium in Wangxiang. At that time, Zhu Youlin, the former second squad leader of the sixth team in our district, was dismissed from his position due to the case. He was ordered to strictly investigate the sixth team. Later, according to Qian A'gen and Yao Renfu, two people involved in the case, on April 24th, they seized more than 400 packages of opium from A'gen's boat on a pig boat outside Changshu City. Later, Zhu Youlin transferred the goods to another boat and transported them to the south bridge of Dangkou. Yao Renfu was entrusted by Zhu Youlin to sell the goods to A'tu and the old woman, etc. Because the case was serious, our district immediately approved the Ministry of Civil Affairs to order Zhu Youlin and Xiao Mingqi to be arrested and bring them to justice. The arrested criminals were sent to the Wuxi County Government for interrogation and judgment according to the law. Therefore, the case was reported by the chief of our district, the chief of our district broke the case, and our chief of the district approved the Ministry of Civil Affairs to arrest the main criminals and send the arrested criminals to the county for legal proceedings. The facts are there and cannot be concealed. What is the basis for saying that he was released in exchange for a bribe? If you can point out concrete evidence, then I will not shirk my responsibility. If it is a false accusation, then I will investigate and find out the truth. As for the plaintiff Yang Bingsheng, our district has searched the register and there is no such person. It can be inferred that if there is indeed a Yang Bingsheng who filed a complaint with the High Court, then it will not be difficult to find out the truth when he is subpoenaed according to the law. I hereby publish this statement and ask you to publish it in the letter column. Mao Mujun, Chief of the Second District of Jiangsu Water Police, December 12th.

Order from the Jiangsu Provincial Government to the Department of Education 85

Two research groups are not legally compliant.

Both are legal entities, not natural persons.

Jiangsu Provincial Government Order No. 7550 to the Department of Education: For notification to the commissioner, the case was approved by the Jiangsu Provincial Party Affairs Consolidation Committee in a letter stating that the Jiangsu Provincial Secondary School Education Research Association (Xue Deyu, et al.) and the Jiangsu Social Education Research Association (Liu Jihong, et al.) have successively submitted their articles of association and requested approval for registration. The association should consider that the organizational units of the two groups, one being provincial secondary schools and the other being provincial social education institutions, are both legal entities and not natural persons. According to the Social Groups Organization Act and the Cultural Groups Organization Guidelines, there is no provision for legal entities to be members. This matter concerns the legal system and cannot be decided arbitrarily. The Central Training Department was asked for instructions. The reply stated that the Cultural Groups Organization Guidelines do not have a provision for legal entities to organize groups. The organization of the Jiangsu Provincial Secondary School Education Research Association and the Jiangsu Provincial Social Education Research Association, both of which use legal entities as organizational units, is not legally compliant and cannot be approved. You should be notified and instructed to notify separately. This order, etc., should be replied to separately and forwarded for reference.

Former Supervisor of Students Studying in Japan 86

Wang Keren's Accounting Unclear; Ministry of Education Orders New Supervisor Liu to Report in Detail: Former Supervisor of Students Studying in Japan, Wang Keren, when passing through Shanghai on his way back to the country this time, gave a speech detailing the disputes concerning students studying in East Asia. After arriving in Beijing on the 9th, Wang immediately went to the Ministry of Education to meet with Vice Minister Liu Dabai, reporting on the handover of supervisory duties to the newly appointed Liu Suichang. Wang mentioned that the Ministry of Education had approved the allocation of 10,000 yuan in national currency from the Chong fund as travel expenses for students from Hunan and Guangxi provinces. He had previously submitted a request to Minister Jiang and Division Chief Sun, requesting the same treatment for government-funded students, which had been approved. Therefore, he had provided the same subsidies to government-funded students. Vice Minister Liu stated that although Wang had made this request previously, it had not been officially approved. The so-called "already approved" was clearly a misunderstanding. Wang also went to the Ministry of Education yesterday to explain the allocation of these funds, stating that he would take responsibility and compensate for any errors. Yesterday, the Ministry of Education issued an order to the new Supervisor of Students Studying in Japan, Liu Suichang, ordering him to investigate Wang's handover situation. The original order stated: "After reviewing the report that former Supervisor Wang's accounts were unclear and had been rejected by the Ministry, when the Ministry approved the resignation of the former Supervisor, it repeatedly ordered that he not be allowed to return to the country until the handover was clear, and instructed the Supervisor to verify each item against the case files. All items not approved for write-off by the Ministry should be calculated clearly before acceptance. Later, based on a telegram stating that the procedures had not been completed, the telegram replied that acceptance was not allowed. Now, after reading various newspapers such as Shen Xin Shi Shi on the 9th of this month, which contained the Supervisor's remarks after returning to the country, and according to reports from Ministry staff that the former Supervisor had indeed left his post and returned to the country, while the Ministry had not received any report from the Supervisor or former Supervisor Wang regarding the handover, and according to a telegram from the manager of students studying in Japan stating that Wang Keren was engaged in even worse embezzlement and corruption than Jiang, and had returned to the country without a clear handover, it is requested that he be detained and dealt with according to the law. Ascertain whether former Supervisor Wang has completed the handover clearly and whether the Supervisor has formally accepted it, and report in detail." This order is issued to this city.

Results of the Four University Mandarin Debate 90

Fudan Wins First Place Overall: The preliminary rounds of the Mandarin Debate Competition among Fudan, Guanghua, Jiaotong, and Jinan Universities were held at the end of last month. The results were that Jiaotong narrowly defeated Guanghua, and Fudan defeated Jinan. Fudan and Jiaotong Universities thus obtained the right to compete in the finals. It is learned that the finals were held at 3 PM on the 12th (the day before yesterday) in the Wen Zhi Hall of Jiaotong University. The chairman was Li Zhaohuan, President of Jiaotong University. The representatives from Jiaotong were Liu Xuantian, Yu Ming, and Huang Kuanzhao. The topic of the debate was "The Existing Universities in Shanghai Should Find Ways to Merge into One Large-Scale University." Fudan argued for the affirmative, and Jiaotong argued for the negative. As a result, Fudan won first place in the overall team score and was awarded a victory flag. Chen Yongcheng from Fudan also won first place individually and was awarded a silver cup. Peng Qixin from Fudan won second place individually and was awarded a silver shield. Huang Kuanzhao from Jiaotong won third place individually and was awarded a silver object. Wang Yunwu also gave a humorous speech while calculating the scores.

Jinan Retains Jiangnan University Football Championship 93

Decisive Victory Over Jiaotong by Nine to Zero: Jiangnan University Championship Won for Third Consecutive Year: Tens of Thousands of Fans Flock to Zhenru Town; Happy to Watch to the End: Flags and banners filled the field, war drums shook the sky, the crowds were mountainous, and the songs were earth-shattering. This was a true depiction of the meeting between Jinan and Jiaotong Universities in Zhenru Town yesterday, and no less grand than the encounter between Nanyang and St. John's on Mackenzie Road in the past. When the whistle blew, the great battle began. The superior defeated the inferior, and the strong defeated the weak. When the ninety minutes were up, the score was settled. As a result, Jinan won by nine goals, continuing to hold the Jiangnan University Championship for the third year.

Jinan Triumphs in Jiangnan for the Third Time 94

The Jinan Football Team has won the Jiangnan Football Championship for two consecutive years. Since the start of this year's competition, they have defeated Guanghua, overcome Zhonggong, and defeated Fudan. Yesterday, they also won decisively against Jiaotong. Thus, the championship of Jiangnan has been held by Jinan for the third time. Jiaotong came in second. The results of each school this year are as follows: School Name | Matches Played | Wins | Losses | Draws | Goals For | Goals Against | Points Jinan | 4 | 4 | 0 | 0 | 32 | 2 | 8 Jiaotong | 4 | 2 | 1 | 1 | 9 | 11 | 5 Guanghua | 4 | 2 | 2 | 0 | 6 | 8 | 4 Fudan | 4 | 1 | 2 | 1 | 4 | 16 | 3 Zhonggong | 4 | 0 | 4 | 0 | 3 | 17 | 0 (1) Each Has Their Own Skills in Art: Goalkeepers: The circumstances and hardships of the goalkeepers of both teams were different. Jiaotong's Li Chuanxin was physically strong and had a firm will. Only two of the nine goals conceded could be blamed on him. The rest were the result of shots taken within five steps, beyond his ability to stop. Li's weakness was a lack of agility in turning and a lack of speed in his hands. Liang Guanlian, who guarded Jinan's goal, was as steady as Mount Tai and had no opportunity to display his talents. The defense was as solid as a city of gold and iron, and even flying birds could not cross it. He encountered two major dangers in his life, but almost ruined things because of complacency in a safe situation, showing off his skills, which was not appreciated by the wise. Jinan and Jiaotong Full Team Members (Photo by Ye Changlie) Inside Line: Jinan's inside line was extremely reliable. Their feet were firm and their positioning was appropriate. Jiang was known for his courage and Feng for his skill. The enemy had no way to sneak through. In the second half, the inside line often stayed in the opponent's area, using defense as a pretext for attack. Whenever the opponent gained momentum and counterattacked, the two were always able to turn around and deal with the situation with ease. Jiaotong's Wang and Chen also had good defensive skills. Wang was especially known for his composure, but under strong pressure from the opponent, he was ultimately unable to cope. His weakness was that he often hesitated to move forward, allowing the enemy to penetrate deep. Center Line: Jiaotong's major defeat was due to the center line. Individually, center back Yang Xinghua was able to loyally fulfill his duties, rushing out to obstruct the attack, but left and right Cheng and Shen did not move properly, leaving many gaps. The entire line was unable to follow the forwards to provide assistance, so the five forwards often failed halfway. In comparison, Jinan was completely different. Zhuang Shihong was the center back, supported by Lin Songfa and Liang Shutang. The three moved quickly and were able to attack and defend equally. The momentum of the forwards was thus greater, and the defense was more solid. It was difficult to distinguish the skills of the three. After Zhuang was injured and left the field, Liang took over Zhuang's position and Yang Baomiao took over Liang's position. After Liang's position changed, he was still impressive. Forward Line: Jinan was superior in terms of order and strength, but Jiaotong was also nimble and skillful. Fei Fuxu made several dangerous attempts, and Liu Ximeng took the lead and was very active. The left and right inside forwards contributed a lot by advancing and retreating according to the situation, but the right wing's performance was disappointing. In the first twenty minutes, they marched boldly to the distant front, but when the center defenders Li Xinchuan saved a ball (photo by this newspaper), the weak points of the line were exposed, and they did not attack much. It is said that the entire line was stationed in the territory, making a final effort seven minutes before the end. They rushed out like swift horses and pounced on the enemy's goal, but were offside and ineffective. Even though it was ineffective, it was still a pleasure to smell the meat even though they did not eat it. Jinan's five forwards were like dragons and tigers, and their imposing manner was intimidating. Wherever they went, the enemy was defeated. Their excellent cooperation and accurate shooting were amazing. Although the nine goals were due to the kicks, the assistance of their teammates could not be ignored. Dai scored four goals, Chen Zhenhe and Fu Hexuan scored two goals each, and Luo Haiguang scored one goal. Only Mei Hongbao and Tong Rongwen did not score.
