Local News

Shanghai to Organize 101

Pacification and Rehabilitation Branch

Discussions on Jiangsu Pacification and Rehabilitation

Since the National Government specially appointed Zhang Zhijiang as the Director of Jiangsu Pacification, it has aroused the attention and expectations of the people of Jiangsu Province. Yesterday, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce specially convened all executive and supervisory committee members to discuss measures for pacification and rehabilitation, and invited Mu Ouchu, Vice Minister of Industry and Commerce, to attend the meeting and report. Attendees included Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Wu Zhihao, Lu Qisheng, Xu Jilu, Fang Jiaobo, Lu Fengzhu, Ma Jiliang, Ye Huijun, Luo Qinghua, Chen Songyuan, Yan Esheng, Zheng Chengqing, etc. After Chairman Wang Xiaolai respectfully read the will, Vice Minister Mu reported, stating that he was attending today as a citizen of Jiangsu to report on the issue of Jiangsu pacification. The people of Su Province have suffered from banditry for a long time. After this military stabilization, the government is determined to suppress bandits. The Jiangsu part has specially appointed Zhang Zhijiang as the Pacification Director. Since the announcement of this order, the Jiangsu compatriots in Beijing have appointed Wu Zhihui, Niu Yongjian, Di Ying, Gao Lingbai, Zhu Wenzhong, and others, including himself, as representatives to express their welcome to Director Zhang and express their willingness to cooperate with the government on the part of the people. The negative aspects of pacification and rehabilitation are to organize Qingxiang Baojia, and the positive aspects are: (1) to raise large sums of money to purchase seeds, agricultural tools, and plowing cattle, and distribute them to farmers in the disaster-stricken areas of northern Jiangsu; (2) to request the Farmers Bank and various banks in Shanghai to bring capital and establish farmers' mortgage loan agencies in the disaster-stricken towns of northern Jiangsu so that farmers do not feel exhausted. On the one hand, it is suggested that the provincial government speed up the construction of a ring road along the Taihu Lake, which is beneficial for suppressing bandits and exporting agricultural products. In northern Jiangsu, the construction of Wan Gong Dike can reduce the scourge of bandits. However, road and dike construction is the responsibility of the government, while fundraising, seed distribution, and the establishment of banks rely on the assistance of the business community, because local security is most related to the development of industry and commerce. Now, the wheat in Su Province this year is not enough to be planted. Planting spring wheat should be done in January and February. If preparations are not made now, it may be too late. Nanjing has already planned to establish a Jiangsu Pacification and Rehabilitation Association, and it is hoped that branches will be set up everywhere in the future to achieve effective results. Shanghai is the commercial center, and the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce has the ability to call on a high level and should also have the willingness to assist in pacification. Therefore, it is highly hoped that the Shanghai branch will be organized by the gentlemen of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and at the same time, efforts should be made to raise donations to purchase seeds and establish banks. If everyone does their best, success will be easy. After detailed discussions by Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, and Wu Zhihao, they unanimously expressed that the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce should do its best to assist the government in handling the pacification of Su Province. As for the organization of a pacification and rehabilitation branch, it should be discussed and convened after the Nanjing side has drafted various rules and regulations.

Water Price Increase Case 102

Mediation Begins

The Ministry of Foreign Affairs telegraphed the office to negotiate

Please advise users to wait quietly for a resolution

The Public Works Department will hold a board meeting tomorrow

Mediation will take place at the British Consulate on the 16th

The dispute over the water company's price increase is becoming increasingly serious. The company is threatening to cut off the water supply, and the public's attitude is becoming increasingly fierce. After receiving a telegram from the Chinese Ratepayers Association in the Concession, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs telegraphed the Shanghai office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs yesterday, ordering it to quickly contact the Public Works Department and the British Consul General to handle the matter peacefully. The water company should be quickly ordered to immediately restore the water supply and not to use the high-pressure tactic of cutting off the water supply again, and to persuade users to remain calm and wait for a peaceful resolution. After detailed consultations between Directors Chen Shiguang and Liu Yunfang, it was decided to first consult with the British Consul General, B. G. Tours, and the Chairman of the Public Works Department, McDonald. At 8:00 PM last night, British Counselor Eggland hosted a banquet for the British Far East Economic Survey Group at the Cathay Hotel. The British Consul General and the Chairman of the Public Works Department were present, and Chen and Liu were also invited to attend. The two sides then met and discussed separately. The British Consul General and others agreed to the peaceful proposal and promised to notify the water company to restore the water supply. According to McDonald, the Public Works Department has scheduled a special board meeting for 4:30 PM next Monday (the 15th) to discuss the matter specifically. At the same time, the British Consul General also agreed with Liu Yunfang to convene representatives of the water company at the British Consulate at 10:00 AM on the 16th for a three-party mediation. The various news heard yesterday are compiled as follows:

The Ratepayers Association sends a letter of condolences to the households whose water has been cut off

Yesterday, the Ratepayers Association sent letters to Zhang Tiankai, a resident of Kang Nao Road, and the Huashang Villa, whose water supply was cut off by the water company, as follows: (1) Letter to Zhang Tiankai, stating that the association received a report from your representative on the afternoon of December 10 and a letter from you on December 11. The Shanghai Water Company, a British company, disregarding humanitarianism and the principles of public utilities, cut off the water supply to your residence on the 10th of this month in order to achieve the purpose of forcing a price increase. It is shocking to learn that the company's tyrannical behavior dares to act arbitrarily within our country's territory. In addition to telegraphing the government to handle the matter and negotiating with the Public Works Department to fulfill its responsibility to supply water, we hope that you will inform us of the situation at any time. (2) Letter to Huang Chunrong, acting on behalf of the Huashang Villa Company, stating that the association received a letter from you on December 11 reporting that the Shanghai Water Company, a British company, closed the main water supply valves for houses 1051 to 1055, Changchun Lane, Peng Road, in order to force a price increase. This is shocking. The opposition to the water company's price increase is the public opinion of all industries and residents, and the responsibility for paying the water bill is not directly borne by your company. The company's anger at your company, which endangers the lives of all residents, is even more of a shameless act of bullying the weak. The company's disregard for humanitarianism and the destruction of the principles of public utilities is extremely barbaric. Your company's fearlessness in the face of tyranny in order to seek justice is commendable and admirable. In addition to telegraphing the government to handle the matter and negotiating with the Public Works Department to fulfill its responsibility to supply water, we are sending this letter to express our respect and hope that you will take note of it and inform us of the situation at any time.

Research on the issue of replacing water meters

Jones, an official of the Public Works Department, stated yesterday that the only way to break the current impasse of the price increase is for the water company to install water meters, and that the Public Works Department has also agreed to this in principle. A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency believes that it is worth studying whether replacing water meters will benefit users. He specially visited Yan Esheng, Executive Committee Member and Secretary of the Chinese Ratepayers Association. According to his statement, the water company has planned to replace water meters for a long time. This matter is very beneficial to the company, but it will definitely increase the burden on ordinary citizens. The direct costs of tap water, excluding indirect costs such as interest rates and depreciation, are an average of 18 cents per 1,000 gallons. The water company charges an average of 23.1 cents per 1,000 gallons for those who pay according to rent and 43.3 cents per 1,000 gallons for those who pay according to water meters. If the company implements a 25% price increase, those who pay according to water meters will pay 54.1 cents per 1,000 gallons. If the company replaces all water meters, ordinary citizens will have to jump from a burden of 23.1 cents per 1,000 gallons to 54.1 cents per 1,000 gallons. What is even more noteworthy is that when water bills are calculated according to rent, they are paid by the landlord. If water meters are replaced, the water bill will be paid by the tenant, just like with electricity. At the same time, landlords will not reduce rent due to the replacement of water meters. From this perspective, not only will ordinary citizens' burden increase from 23.1 cents per 1,000 gallons to 54.1 cents per 1,000 gallons when water meters are replaced, but those who do not bear the water bill will have to bear 54.1 cents per 1,000 gallons in the future. Concession residents account for the majority of the population, so if the company implements the replacement of water meters, the asset class will benefit, while ordinary civilians will suffer. Furthermore, if we compare Chinese and foreign residents, foreigners live in tall Western-style houses with high rents but do not use much water, while Chinese people are the opposite. As a result, foreigners will benefit, while Chinese people will suffer. This issue is very important, and we must give it serious consideration and attention for the sake of ordinary Chinese citizens. According to the water company's calculations, it will cost no more than 2 to 3 million yuan to replace water meters in three years, about 1 million yuan is enough. Jones also said that the company only cut off the water supply to two households because they were three months in arrears, which is also a one-sided statement. The two households are willing to pay the water bill at the old price, but the company refuses to accept it. The company must calculate according to the increased price, but the two households refuse to pay, so the company cut off the water supply. It can be seen that the water supply to the two households was cut off not simply because of arrears, but also because of the price increase issue. Jones said that only these two households have been cut off, and perhaps he thinks that this is still too few. He does not know that if these two households can be cut off, then every household can be cut off, and by extension, the water supply to all concession users can be cut off. This is evidenced by the threatening letters issued by the water company to each household, giving them a deadline to pay or else the water supply will be cut off. Furthermore, imperialists often demanded that the Chinese government cede territory and pay reparations for the killing of one or two missionaries. For example, when Qingdao was forcibly leased, only two missionaries were killed in Shandong. Why didn't they say that only two foreign missionaries were killed? Jones once sent a letter to the Ratepayers Association acknowledging that the water company's cut-off of the water supply was justified. If other incidents occur due to the cut-off of the water supply in the future, Jones should bear full responsibility.

The Real Estate Association held an emergency meeting yesterday

The Shanghai Real Estate Association held an emergency meeting at 4:00 PM yesterday because the water company's cut-off of the water supply is related to the livelihood of millions of residents. All members attended the meeting, and Yan Yanfang was elected as chairman. The chairman reported that the Shanghai Water Company's cut-off of the water supply is a matter of great importance, endangering the lives of residents. The purpose of today's meeting is to ask all members to put forward as many measures as possible so that the association can negotiate. Then, the meeting discussed the agenda items: (1) Send a letter to the Public Works Department ordering the water company to restore the original state and continue to supply water as a prerequisite. The motion was passed. (2) Omitted. (3) Send a letter to the Chinese members of the Public Works Department urging them to strive for the cancellation of the water price increase and the revision of the contract at the special meeting. The motion was passed. (4) The letter will not be drafted today and will be published tomorrow. The motion was passed. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM.

Yesterday 103

Chu Minyi Returns to China

Warm welcome from all walks of life

Chu Minyi, the chief representative of the National Government to the Belgian Centennial Exposition, returned to China yesterday afternoon at 6:00 PM on the Japanese mail ship Shunyo Maru, accompanied by his secretary Zhou Shida. Those who went to the Huangpu Wharf to welcome him were extremely enthusiastic. The situation is recorded as follows:

Grand welcome

First, the preparatory committee for the welcome of Mr. Chu Minyi, the representative of the National Government, was organized by fellow villagers from Huzhou. Later, many more people joined in, about 30 organizations and more than 100 people. The preparatory committee erected a decorated archway at the Huangpu Wharf, with the words "Welcome Mr. Chu Minyi Back to China" written horizontally on it, and a couplet on the side that read, "The name of Bowang remains in the remote areas, and the prosperity of Shen Hao shakes the world." A large gasoline lamp was hung below the horizontal plaque, which was extremely bright and dazzling. Many national flags were also hung, fluttering in the wind. In addition, there were dozens of colored silk flags embroidered with the words "Welcome Mr. Chu Minyi, Representative of the National Government, Back to China," which were particularly pleasing to the eye. In addition, the New Pharmaceutical Industry Association, the Pharmacists Association, Southeast Medical University, the Sino-French National Industrial College, and the Sino-French University Pharmaceutical Training School also had many large white flags and small triangular flags.

Number of welcomers

The organizations that went to the wharf to welcome him included the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Sino-Belgian Boxer Indemnity Committee, the Bankers Association, the Health Construction Committee, the Medical and Pharmaceutical Review Society, the Shanghai National Martial Arts Hall, the Global Chinese Students Association, the Dahua Hospital, the Shanghai Civilian Hospital, the Labor Hospital, the Chinese Hygiene Society, the Times Youth Society, the Tongde Medical Society, the Chinese National Products Federation, the New Pharmaceutical Industry Association, the Pharmacists Association, the Sino-French National Industrial School, the Pharmaceutical Training School, the Labor University, Southeast Medical University, and the Zhongxing Elementary School. Individuals included Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yiting, Lin Kanghou, Lu Liankui, Shao Ruoxin, Yuan Liangzhou, Jiang Xiahun, Song Wusheng, Nong Ruhui, Tian Shoucheng, Chen Gonglu, Zhang Shewo, and Hui Ning School Jiang Paihua, Xu Huanren, Xu Dechen, and Jiang Zhongxi, and over 2,000 other people. Mr. Chu's father, Xing Tian, who is already 80 years old with white hair and beard, and his wife and daughters also came to the shore to greet him.

Songs and music

As the Shunyo Maru approached the wharf, the military band played military music, and the students of the Central School sang welcome songs, mixed with the sound of waving hats and hands. The torches of the photography company and the sound of the sailors mooring the ship were all presented to the eardrums.

Large film

The Mingxing Film Company brought a motion picture camera with torches to film. Whenever Chu Minyi stood on the ship's edge, crossed the ship, went down to the pier, or shook hands with the welcomers, it was all captured on film. In addition, many reporters and photographers from various newspapers and photo studios went to take pictures. Chu Minyi also carried a camera with him and took pictures along the way.

Representatives board the ship

After the ship was docked, the representatives who came to welcome him originally planned to send ten people to board the ship to welcome him, but as soon as the gangway was arranged, Chu Minyi disembarked. Moreover, because there were too many people, it was not easy to push through the crowd to board the ship, so although representatives were sent, they did not board the ship.

Rice stores posted holiday dates

Silk factories agreed to have four days off

A public decision was made that each industry would have four days off for the New Year. Next, the meeting discussed the revision of the distribution plan for the public debt relief of the industry. After careful discussion by the public, the meeting adjourned after 6:00 PM.

The Public Security Bureau should take the lead in advocating

Shanghai Public Security Bureau Order Zhengzi No. 2628 said: In order to comply with the matter, it was found that the measures for promoting the national calendar New Year had been ordered to be followed in accordance with the Municipal Government Order No. 6543. It was found that the first item of the first article of the aforementioned measures stated that ancestor worship, New Year's Eve dinners, and spring banquets should all be changed to the end and beginning of the national calendar year. All internal and external staff of our bureau should take the lead in advocating and earnestly follow the order, and should not continue to follow the old habits and violate the order. In addition to distributing the order, the district leader should be ordered to comply with the order and pass it on to his subordinates for compliance. This order was issued on December 13, 19th year of the Republic of China by Director Yuan Liang.

Xiong Shihui and Yang Yongtai 105

Their injuries showed improvement yesterday

Yang is scheduled to undergo surgery on the 15th

Bian's coffin was escorted back to his hometown yesterday

Xiong Shihui, commander of the Songhu Garrison, and Yang Yongtai, a major general and advisor at headquarters, both showed improvement in their injuries yesterday. However, Yang's surgery using X-rays is still pending. The situation yesterday is recorded below:

Xiong's condition

The orthopedic hospital issued a report in the morning and afternoon, saying: (1) He slept soundly for six hours on the 12th, and his condition improved again on the morning of the 13th. Dean Niu Huisheng borrowed the doctors Zeng Baohan and Chen Jiayu to change the dressing on the injured area, and there were no changes. He also asked Dr. Cao Chentao to check his kidneys, and there were also no changes. His temperature was 99 degrees, his pulse was 84, and his respiration was 20. Dr. Niu said that it was about the same as a normal person. (2) In the afternoon, Dr. Niu Huilin inspected Commander Xiong's condition, and there were no changes. He slept soundly for two hours. After waking up, he ate chicken porridge and pigeon soup. His temperature was 100, his pulse was 84, and his respiration was 20. The Ministry of Finance sent a representative, Hu Lansheng, to the orthopedic hospital yesterday afternoon to visit Xiong in his ward. Xiong nodded and thanked him and talked briefly before Hu left. Yang's symptoms

Trade Regulations Issue 108

The Ministry of Industry and Commerce Asks the Executive Yuan for Approval　　Various Industries Again Petition Vice Minister Mu　　The Trade Regulations Issue that the Shanghai Municipal Various Industries Guilds Are Striving For, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce Submits to the Executive Yuan Asking for Approval, Yesterday Various Industries Also Sent Representatives to Petition Vice Minister Mu of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. The Situation is Recorded Separately as Follows:

(1) Instructions from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce

The Various Industries Safeguarding Trade Regulations Committee Received Yesterday Instruction No. 14438 from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, which opened with a telegram stating that the general assembly of representatives from various industries had unanimously resolved on trade regulations and had again telegraphed the ministry to swiftly implement them, requesting review and compliance. This was delegated to the telegram branch. The telegram stated that the trade regulations case had been submitted to the Executive Yuan for consideration of the three measures proposed by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs in the National Industry and Commerce Conference proposal. This was to be acknowledged. It was also heard that Minister Kong recently sent a letter to a certain well-known figure in Shanghai business circles, roughly stating that the trade regulations issue was expected to be approved by the Executive Yuan.

(2) Situation of Petitioning Vice Minister Mu

The Various Industries Guilds, upon hearing the news that Vice Minister Mu Ouchu of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce would attend the Appeasement Conference convened by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, sent representatives to petition Vice Minister Mu. Representatives from more than 160 guilds, including the Chinese Soap Industry, Coal Industry, Timber Industry, Silk Industry, Paint Industry, Sauce Garden Industry, Chinese Woolen Fabric Factory Industry, Transportation Industry, and Medicinal Materials Industry, totaling more than 300 people, including Mao Chunpu, Luo Zheng, Chen Weiwen, and Lu Wenzhu, held petition banners, and the venue was plastered with slogans, creating a tense atmosphere. At around 4:00 PM, Vice Minister Mu Ouchu of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce arrived at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Committee Room. Representatives from various industries publicly elected Luo Qinghua, Ye Jiaxing, Ge Yanqing, and Qiu Liangyu, along with five other representatives, to lead the audience. The representatives requested Vice Minister Mu to report to the representatives of various industries in the hall on the process and purpose of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce rejecting the trade regulations. Mr. Mu stated that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce had already been ordered to conclude and that he himself was attending the Appeasement Conference today and could not come out to report to the public. The representatives then vehemently stated the importance of trade regulations, arguing that Vice Minister Mu, being a Shanghai merchant by origin, should provide guarantees for the commercial sector, and that the rejection of trade regulations during Vice Minister Mu's term was regrettable. They hoped for more support in the future and requested his presence to address the representatives of various industries on the rejection process. Vice Minister Mu replied that regardless of his future position, he would ask Minister Kong of the Ministry of Industries and relevant departments to find ways to maintain them and prevent the representatives of various industries from being disappointed. While both sides were at a standstill, Municipal Chamber of Commerce Standing Committee member Wang Yansong was present and said that trade regulations were the lifeblood of merchants, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce should strive for them. Moreover, since Vice Minister Mu had already agreed to forward the request, the representatives could wait quietly for good news. At this point, the representatives then took their leave.

(3) Resolutions on Two Temporary Proposals

After the representatives of various industries completed their petition, Luo Qinghua, one of the five representatives, was elected to report on the situation of petitioning Vice Minister Mu and to resolve on two temporary proposals: (1) Send a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward to the Bureau of Social Affairs that all members of the same industry must join the industry guild, and the industry guild must join the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. (2) Telegraph the Executive Yuan to swiftly urge the implementation of the trade regulations of various industries passed by the National Industry and Commerce Conference, regardless of whether members have joined the guild or not, all members of the same industry must abide by the regulations uniformly.

(4) Send a Letter to Minister Kong Asking for Approval

The Safeguarding Trade Regulations Committee organized by the Various Industries Guilds held its seventh committee meeting on the 11th, publicly electing Zheng Chengqing and other representatives to request Minister Kong of the Ministry of Industries to dismiss his intention to resign. It was heard that Minister Kong had reluctantly agreed to take office, and a special letter was sent to express their love and support and to request approval of the trade regulations (abbreviated title). It is said that our association previously heard that the respected director was honorably transferred to the Ministry of Industries and sent a telegram to congratulate him. Then we heard that the respected director had the intention of retiring and immediately telegraphed the National Government on an auspicious day to grant a retention order. At the seventh committee meeting yesterday, Zheng Chengqing, Ye Jiaxing, Sun Choucheng, and other representatives were appointed to approach him and earnestly request him to dismiss his intention to resign, fearing that the matter might be presumptuous, so we specially requested Director Zhao Jinqing to act as an intermediary. Director Zhao informed us that the director had already reluctantly agreed to take office due to the retention of all parties, so it is not appropriate to disturb his peace of mind. We hereby send a letter to express our love and support. Only the trade regulations of various industries are the foundation of the survival of the industry guilds and the key to the rise and fall of the industry. After the respected director takes office, we hope that he will conform to public opinion and swiftly approve and implement the case that all members of the same industry, whether they have joined the guild or not, must abide by the trade regulations. Then all merchants and people will forever feel the great virtue without limit.

Local Court Burned Opium Yesterday 110

The Shanghai Local Court Procuratorate scheduled to burn the opium and poisons confiscated in the first half of the 19th year yesterday. On the scheduled date yesterday, the court erected a mat shed in front of the detention center for the supervisors to stay. In the afternoon at 2 PM, representatives from various agencies, groups, and party departments arrived one after another, including Yang Zhaoxin and Chen Jingzhai from the Ministry of Justice, Yu Zongjian from the Higher Court, Zhang Yi from the Municipal Party Department, Zhang Yinhuai from the Municipal Government, Zhu Yuntao from the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Chen Jiannan from the County Party Department, Chen Guozhen from the County Public Security Bureau, He Xiaosong from the Jianghai Customs, Yu Ding from the Special Zone Local Court, Wang Yun from the Anti-Drug Association, and Ms. Zhou Chucai. They were welcomed by Chief Prosecutor Liu Maochu and led to the opium burning field. Prosecutor Lei Renlong and the clerks distributed a list of confiscated poisons, ordering Police Chief Yang Deshan and Police Officers Chen and Chen Junfang to supervise the bailiffs to weigh each item of opium, opium paste, red pills, and other poisons, dismantle them one by one, and then stack them with pine wood, pour kerosene, sprinkle salt, and set them on fire. It was not until 4 PM that the event concluded. This time, a total of 5,301.5 taels of opium, 49 catties and 4 taels of opium materials, 112 catties of red pills, 31 catties and 12.6 taels of morphine, 8 catties and 4 taels of heroin, and 2,925 pieces of opium paraphernalia and sundries were burned. After the burning, police were dispatched to guard the ashes strictly until the next day, when they were scattered and sunk in the Huangpu River to clear the poisonous atmosphere.

Shanghai Municipal Council 111

Decides to Form a Public Debt Custodian Committee, According to the Shanghai Times, in order to fulfill the declaration of selling the electricity department, the Public Concession Municipal Council has decided to form a Municipal Council Public Debt Custodian Committee, which will be established soon to protect the interests of bond purchasers. The committee members will be appointed from Westerners with good reputation. All public debts due for redemption before 1933 will be managed by the committee. The purchase price paid by the Shanghai Power Company, designated for debt repayment, will also be handed over to the committee for safekeeping. In this way, all public debts of the Municipal Council can be repaid by the end of 1933, and new public debts will be raised again in 1934 to meet the needs of municipal construction. According to the Municipal Council, the public debt issued by the Council is guaranteed by the Council's assets and income. Although the assets have decreased after the sale of the electricity department, the Shanghai Power Company still mortgages all its assets to the Municipal Council until the purchase price of 81 million taels is paid in full. Therefore, the public debt collateral has not actually decreased. According to the sales contract of the electricity department, 36.5 million taels of public debt will be transferred to the Shanghai Power Company for repayment, and the remaining 17.5 million taels will be appropriated by the Municipal Council from the purchase price paid by the company before the end of 1933. Now, in order to consolidate the investment security of bond purchasers, the Municipal Council has organized a custodian committee to keep this debt repayment fund. However, the custodian agreement and charter have not yet been drafted. According to the Municipal Council, in addition to the 54 million taels designated for redeeming public debt from the proceeds of the sale of the electricity department, only 27 million taels remain for all construction needs, such as expanding the West Prison, adding schools, adding police stations and hospitals, expanding canals, widening roads, building incinerators, and other urgent projects. According to the Accounting Office, after all public debts are repaid in 1933, 8 million to 10 million taels of new debt will have to be raised in 1934 to meet urgent needs. If this construction budget can be maintained at 6 million taels per year according to the original plan for the next three years, the remaining proceeds from the sale of the electricity department will be sufficient for application. If no new debt is issued, the patrol donation and other items can also be maintained at the old rate without increasing.

However, the terrain of Tui 35 in Binbei and Jiang Zi embankment of Tui 22 was not convenient to be divided into the Yinhang District. He will ask the two members, Tang and Liu, to attend the next Regional Division Committee meeting to discuss the matter. Therefore, the two members, Tang and Liu, have invited the gentry to talk and explain the above situation.

Beijing-Shanghai Railway 115

New Locomotives Are Sequentially Produced and Operated, The two railway bureaus have recently found that the weather is getting colder and the locomotive traction is insufficient, resulting in frequent delays in train operations, which is inconvenient for travelers. They have specially taken measures to remedy this. On the one hand, the original old locomotives are being repaired as quickly as possible by opening night shifts. On the other hand, four new Pacific-style locomotives that have been transported have been installed and put into operation. One locomotive was installed last Friday and was tested in Wusong with very satisfactory results. The remaining three locomotives can also be installed and put into operation before the 20th of this month. Four more locomotives will be installed in the middle of next month. After this, the problem of train delays can be completely resolved one after another. The railway bureau is still concerned that there may be shortcomings, so it has put forward measures to designate staff from various departments to form a train delay review committee. Any train delay of more than half an hour will be submitted to the committee for review and punishment. Before the train delay problem is completely resolved, each express train will be staffed by one person from the locomotive and rolling stock departments to stand beside the driver to monitor and prevent negligence and delays, and to maintain the reputation of the railway.

Fog Prevents Merchant Ships from Entering and Exiting Sequentially 118

More than 30 ships were prevented from entering and exiting in two days, In the past two days, heavy fog occurred on the sea surface outside the Wusong estuary. Merchant ships coming to Shanghai from various places were prevented from entering and were anchored at sea for safety. There were 18 ships caught in the fog. There were also more than a dozen ships leaving Shanghai that were prevented from sailing due to the fog at the Wusong estuary. The ships on the sea, fearing collision in the fog, sounded their horns all night long, and the sound continued unabated. Yesterday, when the weather turned cold, the fog dissipated, and the waterways were clear, the ships began to enter the Huangpu River, and those leaving Shanghai also sailed yesterday. The ships that were delayed the most were the merchant ships coming to Shanghai from the Yellow Sea. They all entered the port one after another yesterday, and no accidents occurred.

Progress of Dredging the Shentan Shoal at the Wusong Estuary 120

Sends Engineers to Measure, The motion of the Dredging Bureau to dredge the Shentan Shoal (also known as Yinsha) outside the Wusong Estuary has been discussed at the bureau meetings with Chinese and foreign shipping circles twice. It is agreed that in recent years, the displacement tonnage of ships from various countries in the world has doubled, and it often takes a lot of time to bypass the Wusong Estuary, which is a great loss. It is imperative to dig out the Shentan to facilitate navigation. However, this matter is of great importance and the cost is huge. It can only be carried out after sufficient funds are raised. Chinese and foreign shipping circles have mostly agreed to support it, considering that the Shentan survey report refers to the former Technical Committee. It seems that the recent situation of the shoal should be measured in detail to make a practical plan and determine the amount of funding. It was decided to send Oteni, the chief surveyor of the bureau, and Xia Ruifu, the deputy engineer, to lead a team to the Wusong Estuary to conduct a detailed measurement of the Shentan. The base of the Shentan is made of stone or sand, or even has stone roots. It must be measured before construction can begin.

In the Cow Dung

A Male Corpse Horrifyingly Appeared 123

The Face Had Many Knife Wounds, It Was Clearly a Case of Moving the Body After Being Murdered, Yesterday afternoon, an unidentified male corpse was found near the riverbank along Jiaotong Road in Zhabei. Although the deceased was not wearing a long gown, his short shirt and trousers were quite neat, suggesting he might be a respectable merchant. His cheeks had numerous knife wounds, and his neck was tied with a scarf. His chest was stained with fresh blood, and his lower body was naked, with his trousers tangled at his feet. The entire body was deeply buried under a pile of cow dung. Judging from the circumstances, it is presumed that he was stabbed to death, and then his neck was tied with a scarf, and he was carried to the location, covered with cow dung, and deeply buried in the soil, hoping to cover up the tracks. The cause of his death is likely to be murder for money or murder due to adultery. The details are described below:

Falling in a Pool of Blood, Jiaotong Road, about three miles from Shanghai, is a remote area with sparse residents. A few thatched houses are scattered among the fields. The Shanghai-Nanjing Railway is on the left, and the fields are on the right, making it an extremely quiet place. There is a cattle slaughterhouse set up by Fei Xingfa, which consists of three thatched houses and seems to be doing well. In front of the slaughterhouse is a small riverbank where a lot of cow dung is dumped. Yesterday afternoon around 1:00 PM, a scavenger was turning over the discarded dung when he suddenly discovered a male corpse in the middle. Upon closer inspection, he realized that it was a person who had been stabbed to death and was lying in a pool of blood, a horrifying sight. He shouted loudly, and Wang Amin, the manager of the cattle slaughterhouse, who happened to be outside preparing to urinate, saw the scene and immediately reported it to the police station.

The Deceased's Tragic Condition, Shi Zhaoyu, the patrol chief of the Tanziawan Police Station of the Fourth District Sub-bureau, led police officers to investigate and found that the unidentified male corpse was approximately 30 years old. He was wearing a blue serge jacket with a vest, a white short shirt underneath, and white single trousers pulled down to his ankles. He was wearing white socks but no shoes. He had a round head, and his face had six or seven knife wounds. One knife wound was near his right cheekbone, about an inch long. Another knife wound was below his mouth, penetrating his teeth. His left cheek was covered with knife marks, and a knife wound near his ear exposed the flesh and bone. A few broken teeth were left in his mouth, and everything was stained with red blood. A beige scarf with light blue patterns was tied tightly around his neck, and his entire body was buried deeply in the river mud, about three feet deep. His head was resting on the riverbank, and his feet were submerged in the water. Judging by the freshness of the blood, he must have been murdered not long ago. The cause of his death is mostly likely murder for money, as it is now winter, and pig butchers are emerging. It is likely that the murderer did not have a gun and used the method of using a scarf to strangle the neck. He resisted along the way, resulting in him being stabbed to death. Another speculation is that it was murder due to adultery, as the deceased was only wearing a single pair of trousers and was completely naked below the waist. After the investigation, Patrol Chief Shi reported to the sub-bureau, instructing the local warden Liu San to report the case to the court for verification. As the case involves murder, the sub-bureau has strictly ordered its subordinates to arrest the murderer and bring him to justice.

Japanese Man's Grand Swindle 124

Lili Company Suffers Heavy Losses. Shanghai, a place where various people gather, is a mix of good and bad. Deceptive tricks emerge one after another, and foreigners disguising themselves as wealthy to swindle gold jewelry and valuables are not uncommon. Yesterday, a major swindle by a Japanese man occurred at the Lili Company on Wusong Road. The incident was quite unusual, and the reporter has recorded the known details as follows:

Japanese Man Selects Diamond Jewelry: Around 2 PM yesterday afternoon, a handsome Japanese man, approximately 27 or 28 years old, suddenly arrived at the Lili Jewelry Company at 31 Wusong Road. He claimed he wanted to purchase several high-end jewelry items. The shop assistant asked what he needed, and he replied that he was specifically there to select a diamond ring and a platinum rectangular watch. The shop assistant then took out various watches and rings for the Japanese man to choose from. He ultimately selected a diamond ring and a platinum watch. After examining the goods, he suddenly claimed that he only had Japanese currency on him and needed to have it exchanged at his brother's place. He also needed to show the goods to his brother because he was purchasing them on his behalf.

Company Sends Assistant with Jewelry: The Lili Company asked the Japanese man where his brother was located and what his name was. The Japanese man said his brother was the manager of the Osaka Mercantile Steamship Co. at the intersection of Guangdong Road, named Harada. Lili believed him and sent shop assistant Qian Qingfa, carrying the diamond ring and watch, to follow the Japanese man to the Five Horse Road to collect the payment, which seemed quite reliable. Qian accompanied the Japanese man (who did not leave his name) to the Osaka Company. Unexpectedly, upon arriving at the Nisshin building on Guangdong Road (where the Osaka Company was located), the Japanese man played a trick.

False Letter Used to Obtain Watch and Ring: Inside the Nisshin building, the Japanese man suddenly claimed that his brother was in the Osaka office (in a large room on the west side). He told Qian Qingfa that it was inconvenient for him to enter the office and instructed him to wait on a bench outside the Nisshin Company for a moment. As he spoke, he took out an envelope (Chinese style) from his pocket, sealed tightly on both ends. On the outside, it stated that it contained a 500 yen Japanese money order. He handed it to Qian and ordered him to give him the ring and watch so he could show them to his brother for a moment and then come back to exchange the money. Qian thought this was reliable and did not know that there was another gate on Guangdong Road for entering and exiting (according to Qian's statement to the reporter, it was his first time at the Nisshin building and he thought there was only one entrance from the Bund side). Believing that he had the money order and the man was inside the building, he handed over the jewelry.

Man Vanishes Like a Yellow Crane: The Japanese man took the jewelry and walked around the Nisshin counter towards the Osaka Company, but in reality, he did not enter the Osaka office. Instead, he left through the main gate with the stolen goods. Qian waited inside the Nisshin Company for the Japanese man to come and exchange the money. He waited from 2:30 PM until 3:00 PM, but the man did not return. He became increasingly anxious and went to the west side to look for the Japanese man. He saw that the entrance to the Osaka Company was also the main gate. He realized something was wrong and searched everywhere, upstairs and downstairs, but the man had vanished like a yellow crane.

Fake Money Order Discovered: Unable to find the Japanese man, Qian Qingfa went to the Osaka Company to inquire if such a person existed and if there was a person named Harada working there. The Osaka employee replied that there was no employee with that name. Qian realized he had been swindled and quickly opened the money order the Japanese man had given him, only to find a torn piece of old newspaper. Qian was shocked and immediately returned to the company to report the incident. At the same time, he went to the Japanese consulate to report the swindle. The Japanese consulate immediately sent two Japanese detectives with Qian to inquire at Nisshin and Osaka on Guangdong Road if they had seen the swindler. Both companies replied that they had not paid attention, and it was impossible to investigate immediately. They could only slowly search. Lili suffered a significant loss in this swindle. According to Qian Qingfa, the company had been swindled once before, when a Westerner came to purchase jewelry and the store owner personally delivered it, similar to the current situation.

Shaving Off a Mole Hair 125

Barber Shows No Remorse. Stableman Enraged, Gathers Crowd to Cause Trouble.

Fu Aliu, a Yangzhou stableman (also known as Xiaoliuzi) from the horse stable at 38 Great Western Road in Shanghai West, went to the Xinfali Barber Shop at 2054 Jing'an Temple Road on the evening of the 11th to have his face groomed. The barber, Ge Fu, accidentally shaved off a hair from a mole on his face. Fu was enraged and demanded compensation from Ge. Ge showed no remorse, so Fu left in anger. He gathered sixteen of his friends, each wielding axes and iron rulers, and stormed into the Xinfali Barber Shop to confront Ge. Despite attempts to mediate, the enraged group was unreasonable. They dragged Ge outside and beat him severely with axes and iron rulers before scattering. Ge fell to the ground, bleeding profusely. The local police precinct received a report and dispatched officers, who took Ge to the hospital by car. They also began investigating the assailants. The police arrested Fu and accomplices, including stablemen Wang Youcai and Shao Qizai, early the next morning. Yesterday morning, they were brought to the District Court. Ge, injured, also appeared in court to describe the incident, stating that Fu had led a gang to attack him. Fu and the others were evasive. Police lawyer Tu Yaotang requested a postponement. Judge Feng ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody for another seven days for further questioning.

Chopping Zheng Xiangqian with an Axe 126

Sixteen Yuan Eighty in Opium Debts. Two Fingers Severed.

Zheng Xiangqian, a 28-year-old Chaozhou merchant, runs a bean and wheat shop on Min'guo Road and established the Nine Heavens Club in Taiyuan Lane, Zilaihuo Street, in the French Concession. Yesterday morning at 1:30 AM, more than ten thugs armed with pistols and axes broke into the club and chopped Zheng eight times. He immediately fell unconscious. A detailed investigation of the case is summarized below.

Concubine's Opium Debts: Last spring, Zheng began an affair with a Changzhou woman who frequented the club daily. The woman's father was addicted to opium and owed Zhou, who lived at number 253 Yuqing Lane, a total of sixteen yuan and eighty cents in opium debts. When the debt remained unpaid, the woman returned to Changzhou. Several days ago, Zhou sought out the woman and took her cloak, stating he would return it upon payment of the debt. The woman informed Zheng, who sent a tea server from the club to negotiate with Zhou. The cloak was returned after an agreement was made to repay the debt when the woman's father returned to Shanghai from Changzhou. The day before yesterday, Zhou, accompanied by Ma Pi Asi and a person nicknamed "Sixteen," went to Zheng Xiangqian's place to negotiate. Unable to reach an agreement, they left unhappy.

Dozens of Thugs: Yesterday morning at 1:30 AM, Zheng was having congee with his concubine at the club when more than ten thugs armed with pistols and axes stormed into the west room upstairs. Without asking questions, they chopped Zheng eight times (two fingers were severed, and he sustained one cut each to his waist and arm, and two cuts to his lower body). Zheng fell to the ground in agony. The thugs, seeing their goal achieved, fled downstairs.

Report to Police and Search for Criminals: After the incident, Zheng's concubine reported it to the Da Zimingzhong Police Station. The police chief ordered detectives Gu Mengzhou and armed officers to inspect the scene. Zheng was awakened, and the names of the thugs were determined. The police went to Zhou's residence in Yuqing Lane to arrest him, but the thugs had already fled. They could only return to the scene of the crime and send the injured Zheng to Binlong Hospital on Baker Road. It is said that his injuries are severe and life-threatening.

German Man Violates Firearm Regulations 128

Stopped Execution Due to Heart Disease.

Carl Genzow, a 64-year-old German man, was sentenced to two years in prison by the former Provisional Court on June 31 of last year for violating firearm regulations. After entering prison, Carl suffered from heart disease, and any physical exertion caused him to faint. Recently, his condition worsened, and he requested parole from the District Court of the Special District so he could seek medical treatment outside. However, the criminal law stipulates that parole must be requested by the warden of the prison to the Ministry of Justice. The German prisoner's request to the court was not in accordance with the law and was rejected. Now, the prison warden of the prison has reported Carl's condition to the Municipal Council, stating that he has been following prison regulations. They asked if the Special District Court could grant parole. The legal department of the Municipal Council has forwarded the request to the Special District Court. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Cheng Shangfeng held a hearing and brought Carl to court. Judge Cheng first asked the police lawyer if the request was for parole or suspension of the unserved sentence. He noted that parole is clearly stipulated in Article 93 of the Criminal Law, requiring the warden of the prison to request approval from the Ministry of Justice before parole can be granted. Article 485 of the Criminal Procedure Law stipulates that if a prisoner suffers from an illness that could endanger their life if the sentence is carried out, they may request a suspension of execution for medical treatment. After recovery, they must return to prison. Judge Cheng inquired as to which procedure the police were requesting. The lawyer stated that the police were requesting a suspension of execution. Judge Cheng asked if it was true that the Western prison had a discount on the terms of imprisonment, such as a one-year sentence being reduced to eight months. The lawyer replied that although such a practice existed, it was conditional on the prisoner's behavior and not automatically granted. The lawyer claimed, however, that this prisoner had behaved well in prison and the warden supported such a consideration. Judge Cheng ordered the court staff to escort Carl to the medical examiner for examination. The medical examiner reported that Carl was suffering from severe heart disease and that further imprisonment could endanger his life. The court then ordered Carl Genzow to be released on bail of 1,000 yuan in cash and a guarantor from a firm, for medical treatment. After recovery, the guarantor would ensure that he would return to prison to serve the remainder of his sentence upon summons.

Public Notice from the Municipal Public Security Bureau 129

Reissuing 1931 Vehicle Licenses.

The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau issued two public notices yesterday. The first notice concerns the reissuance of various vehicle licenses for 1931, starting from December 25th. Except for cars and trucks, which will be announced separately, the specific regulations are as follows: (1) Before paying the first installment of the 1931 fees, vehicle owners should bring their old licenses to the following locations to exchange for new licenses: cars, motorized bicycles, horse-drawn carriages, and privately owned rickshaws: General Vehicle Office of the Bureau. Dung carts: nearby Vehicle Offices. (2) A license fee must be paid at the time of exchange. The fees are as follows: cars, motorized bicycles, horse-drawn carriages, and privately owned rickshaws: 30 cents per license. Dung carts: 20 cents per license. (3) The license fee for bicycles, including the license plate and license, is 50 cents. The previously designated deposit fee is hereby canceled, and this fee will not be refunded. However, those who obtained old plates for 1930 and return the plates to the Bureau before the end of January 1931, without any damage, will be refunded the previously paid deposit fee of 50 cents. The above points are hereby announced to all vehicle owners. The second notice concerns the reissuance of truck licenses for 1931. The Bureau has decided to start reissuing truck licenses for 1931 on December 25th. At the same time, new numbers will be reissued and new license plates will be issued. All truck owners must take their vehicles to a nearby Vehicle Office of the Bureau before paying the January 1931 monthly fees to have the steel stamp re-applied and obtain a new number, license plate, and 1931 license. A license exchange fee of 20 cents must be paid. Those who have not exchanged their license plates by the end of January 1931 will have their license plate numbers canceled and the original deposit fee confiscated. This notice is hereby announced.

The Taixing'an Bridge and Maojia'bang Bridge in Wusong are essential routes for residents of the northwest countryside of Wusong to reach the town. Freighter Overturns Fishing Boat 136

Fish Vendor Zhang Zhitian Dies Tragically.

At 6:30 AM on the 11th, three fish vendors from Pudong were transporting eight baskets of fresh fish they had purchased from Puxi across the river on a No. 170 rowboat at the China Merchants Bureau Jiangtian Wharf, heading towards the west side of the French warship's pontoon. Suddenly, a freighter towing barges from the Da Lai Company sped north. The rowboat tried to avoid it, but it was too late. The freighter's bow struck the left side of the rowboat. Fish vendor Zhang Zhitian was crushed at the waist. The rowboat overturned, and everyone on board fell into the water. The No. 358 rowboat nearby came to rescue the people in the water. The Da Lai freighter transported Zhang Zhitian to Tongren Hospital for treatment, but he died yesterday morning. Upon hearing the tragic news, Zhang's wife, Tao, reported it to the Water Police. In the afternoon, the police chief ordered detective Huang Songsheng to transport the body from the hospital to the Rescue Bureau to await examination by the court. The shipping company responsible for the accident was ordered to provide generous compensation to the deceased's family. Zhang was 37 years old and from Pudong.

Vegetable Boat Encounters Storm 137

Over 2,000 Cabbages Lost. Lives and Cargo Saved.

Around 5:00 PM the day before yesterday, a storm suddenly broke out. The storm was particularly fierce outside the Wusong estuary. Zhu Changfa, a Chongming boat carrying more than 3,000 cabbages to Songjiang for sale, encountered the sudden storm at the Sanjiakou estuary. The situation was difficult to manage, and there were fifteen passengers on board, including men and women. Seeing that the wind was strong and the boat was tilting, they panicked and cried. The boat owner, seeing the situation was not good, ordered the crew and passengers to throw the cabbages into the sea. After throwing away more than 2,000 cabbages, the boat gradually stabilized. The sails were lowered, and the boat drifted with the wind. The storm subsided until midnight, and they were able to escape the danger. The boat arrived in Wusong around 7:00 AM yesterday morning. According to the boat owner, it was fortunate that they were willing to sacrifice more than 2,000 cabbages to save the lives of over twenty people on board and the cargo. According to Ma, the helmsman of the sand barge, when his boat departed from Liuyao, Chongming, two other vegetable boats departed at the same time. Those two boats also encountered the storm at the estuary, but there has been no news of their arrival in Wusong.

Prosecutor Liu Strives to Defend Sovereignty 138

The case of Russian engineer Qianluosiding injuring a worker with a gun on Yuyuan Road has been reported previously. It is said that the Russian, in order to escape the jurisdiction of the inland court, sued the worker in the Special District Court for obstructing freedom. The Special District Court then requested the extradition from the inland court. Chief Prosecutor Liu Maochu cited Article 17 of our country's criminal procedure and criminal law, which clearly stipulates that if the same case is accepted by two or more courts of the same level, the court that first accepted the case should continue to handle it. A case should not have two trials. Furthermore, the Yuyuan Road area is not within the concession. Although Article 5 of the agreement between the Special District Court states that the court's jurisdiction is unrelated to road construction issues, this case is not related to road construction, and the crime occurred in our country. We cannot easily condone the invasion of our country's legal rights by foreigners. Chief Prosecutor Liu served as a counselor and special envoy of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs several years ago and has extensive knowledge and experience in foreign affairs.

Accidental Killing of Wang Jingtao by Indian Soldiers: An Unresolved Case 144

Widow Pleads for Compensation Wang Mao appeals for 20,000 yuan in compensation Shanghai Municipal Council only willing to provide 100 yuan in relief Wang Jingtao, a local resident living in Wangjiazhai, Yinxiang District, who worked in the leather shoe industry, was returning home at 7:30 PM on March 31st of the 16th year of the Republic of China. He was separated from his house by a field embankment. In front of his house, at the border of the Chinese concession, the Shanghai Municipal Council had erected barbed wire. When Wang attempted to cross the barbed wire, a stationed Indian soldier mistakenly fired two shots, both hitting Wang in vital areas. He died despite medical treatment. Li Jinfu, a judge from the former Provisional Court, confirmed the death and allowed Wang's widow, Wang Mao, to claim the body for coffin preparation. He also instructed her to negotiate with the embassy and report the incident. However, Mao, being an ignorant woman, delayed the matter until now, causing the deceased to suffer in silence and unable to find justice. Currently, Mao has two sons and two daughters who all need to attend school. Moreover, her husband's coffin remains exposed and unburied. Her wages from working in a yarn factory are meager and insufficient to support her family. Therefore, she submitted a petition to Edward, the General Manager of the Shanghai Municipal Council, requesting compensation of 20,000 yuan for Wang's loss of life based on responsibility (Wang earned over 60 yuan per month and, based on a life expectancy of 60 years, the total loss would be 20,000 yuan over 25 years). After receiving the petition, the Shanghai Municipal Council sent personnel to investigate the Donghua Yarn Factory where Mao works and agreed to provide Mao with a relief fund of 100 yuan. Mao refused, stating that her husband was a law-abiding civilian mistakenly killed by an Indian soldier. The Indian soldier was requested by the Shanghai Municipal Council to maintain public security within the concession. Since the Indian soldier caused the accident, the Shanghai Municipal Council should be responsible for compensating the loss of life and providing condolences to the family. Therefore, she rejected the 100 yuan relief fund. Yesterday, she again submitted a petition to Edward and Fessenden, urging them to promptly provide compensation to value human life and uphold justice. It is said that Mao is an old-fashioned woman who highly values etiquette and teaching. She has remained a widow to raise her children, enduring hardship and loneliness, and is praised by relatives and neighbors who sympathize with her.

Free Talk by Binhui

Tan Zhizheng on Returning from Yunnan and Guizhou 155

Yunnan and Guizhou are located in the western frontier, important for our country's border defense. However, due to transportation difficulties, they are often overlooked by our countrymen. Last year, the Ministry of Railways sent specialists to the two provinces to conduct on-site surveys for national railway routes, which took half a year to complete. Recently, Zhang Fuquan, the section chief from Jiaotong University in this city, who was one of the survey specialists, was specially invited to the university to give a lecture on his experiences, which was very interesting. I am recording some of it here, hoping it will be of interest to those who care about border affairs. How to Get There To go from Shanghai to Yunnan, one must pass through French Indochina. First, take a ship from Shanghai to Hong Kong, then from Hong Kong to Haiphong in Indochina, and then take the Yunnan-Vietnam Railway directly to Kunming. To enter Guizhou from Yunnan, one can take a sedan chair from Kunming for about 18 days to reach Guiyang. If starting from Shanghai, one must first go to Chongqing and then take a sedan chair to Guiyang, a journey of 900 li, which takes about 15 days. The transportation can be said to be extremely inconvenient. Sedan chair carriers feel exhausted after traveling 70 li per day. The hardship of living in a sedan chair for more than ten days is indescribable. Characteristics of the Yunnan-Vietnam Railway The Yunnan-Vietnam Railway is 800 li long, slightly longer than the Beijing-Shanghai Railway. However, while the Beijing-Shanghai Railway can be reached in seven or eight hours, the Yunnan-Vietnam Railway takes at least three days. This is because the railway is narrow-gauge and travels very slowly, and it also stops running at night. The most interesting thing is that the railway has as many as 149 tunnels, as if the train is traveling through mountain roads. Special Climate The climate in both provinces is very mild. In Kunming, the highest temperature in summer is only 70 or 80 degrees. At night, one cannot sleep without a cotton quilt. The same is true in Guiyang. However, there is one unique point: once it rains, the climate suddenly becomes cold. There is a local saying: "Four seasons without hot or cold, one rain turns it into winter," which is indeed true. Remarkable Scarcity of Population Due to transportation blockages, the population of the two provinces is extremely sparse. Except for one or two large cities, the remaining county towns have only a few dozen households, which is even smaller than a small village in Jiangsu Province. In recent years, the country has often worried about the increase in population. It should be known that the border areas are the best places for immigration, and the mild climate is especially suitable for southerners.

Understanding Bird Language by Ji Xian 156

My neighbor, Mr. Zhu, is very fond of raising birds, especially parrots. Last month, he happened to visit the Yimiao Temple and bought two parrots from a shop, one male and one female. He loved them very much. Sometimes he would let them fly freely in the wind, enjoying each other's company or making chirping sounds, as if they were conversing. However, Zhu believed that there must be words to understand. Therefore, he separated the male and female parrots. When the male chirped, he would hold a megaphone to the female's ear. After hearing it, the female would flutter her wings, looking for something. Zhu would then pick up the megaphone and listen carefully, and he would hear two phrases, seemingly asking for water and looking for food. Therefore, he would transmit these phrases to the male, and the male would understand, and his actions would be the same as before. Zhu was overjoyed. He predicted that in a few months, he would be able to understand many more phrases. Gongye Chang's ability to understand bird language would not be unique to him.

Just Laugh It Off by Haike 157

Mother: Child, how many apples have you eaten?

Child: I ate three apples, they were very sweet.

Mother: Why didn't you give one to your younger brother when you ate so many by yourself?

Child: I gave him all the seeds from the three apples. He can plant them in the ground and grow a garden of apples next year and eat his fill.

A: I should have come to support you today since you are performing on stage for the disaster relief fundraising event.

B: You are too kind. My skills are not good. I need you to guide me in everything.

A: Unfortunately, I have another very important matter today and cannot come to learn from you. Fortunately, even though my body cannot come, my heart is with you.

B: It's great that your body doesn't have to come, but please buy a ticket for your heart for a special box, 20 yuan each, and donate all the proceeds.

A: You say there are no ghosts in the world?

B: There are definitely no ghosts. Seeing ghosts is a psychological effect.

A: But last night in the yard, I saw a ghost shadow on the wall.

B: What did the ghost shadow look like?

A: It was very scary, like an evil dog standing on its hind legs. After a while, it disappeared.

B: You're mistaken. That was your own shadow.

Never Eating Rice The people of Yunnan, except for the very wealthy who can afford to eat rice, mostly eat corn. The poorest people eat sweet potatoes. Most people never eat rice in their lives. The low standard of living can be imagined.

The Plague of Miasma The greatest disaster in Yunnan is the miasma. People die instantly when they are exposed to it. Where this gas comes from is still uncertain, and there is a lack of preventive measures. Also, both Yunnan and Guizhou provinces are thousands of feet above sea level, which will be a major obstacle to future railway construction.

Abundant Mineral Resources Both provinces have extremely rich mineral resources. Yunnan's antimony is the most famous, and Guizhou's mercury accounts for 9% of the world's production, making it a huge resource. If they can be developed carefully, the natural resources are beyond imagination.

A Bronze Buddha Weighing 63,000 Jin by Zheng Yimei 158

In Nanchang, Jiangxi, there is a temple called Youmin Temple. It was originally Youqing Temple during the Qing Dynasty, but it was renamed to its current name after the Republic of China. In fact, there is a bronze Buddha in the temple, its color dark and old, said to be from the Liang Dynasty. It is more than two zhang tall, and the top of the Buddha and the ridge weigh a total of 63,000 jin. An American archaeologist named Miss Leight visited and wrote a book called "The Beauty of the Orient," calling it the world's first ancient bronze Buddha and attaching a photo to highlight its importance. It is said that a rascal lived in the temple. This rascal, named Jia, extorted money from all sides, and people looked at him with disdain. One day, without wearing pants, he went to the market wearing a long gown and went to a clothing store to buy pants. The clerk showed him a silk pair. Jia put them on to cover himself, as if testing the fit. However, he asked the clerk to bring out more items for him to choose from. Then, they argued about the price, and Jia prepared to leave. The clerk stopped him and said that he had to take off the pants he was wearing to return them. Jia pretended to be angry and said that the pants were originally his own, and how could they be claimed by someone else? Moreover, he only had one pair of pants, and there was no way he could enter the market naked. They argued endlessly, and the onlookers thought Jia was in the right, and the clerk could not defend himself. He also once ate at a noodle shop, but the owner refused to give him credit. Jia resented this. One day, he invited several of his cronies to go to the noodle shop and gorge themselves. After a while, two people suddenly came to the door and started arguing over something, eventually fighting each other. The cronies scattered and fled without paying a single penny. The fighters also ran away. This was a prearranged plan. Jia's bad behavior is too numerous to list. He lived in the temple for many years. Suddenly, one night, he had a dream that the bronze Buddha fell down and crushed his head. Jia woke up in a great fright. From then on, his behavior became erratic, his speech was nonsensical, and he confessed his sins. Not long after, he drowned himself in the river. Therefore, the local people all said that it was the spirit of the bronze Buddha that had brought down the punishment. This is an absurd tale, but we can listen to it with a grain of salt. I suspect it was a neurological issue.

Reflections on Viewing Wang Ronglu's European Painting Exhibition by Yu Jifan 159

The history of the development of Western art can be roughly divided into two major eras: one is the Renaissance period, which lasted for about 150 years in the fourteenth, fifteenth, and sixteenth centuries, centered in Italy and developing to France, the Netherlands, and other places. The main theme was the reverence for ancient art. The other is modern art since the Impressionist era, which began in the nineteenth century and is centered in France.

Travels in Southeast Asia (99) 160

Burma is a Buddhist country. Now the power of national education and local affairs all comes from the monks. The Burmese monks we speak of are not necessarily true monks. Rather, when children of each family reach the age of study, they are sent to temples to be guided by monks in all matters of moral and artistic learning. After several years, they return to their hometown, glorifying their village. It would be better to call them student monks. However, I believe this method is very good. The Datong School can emulate it. While serving as monks, they abandon all desires, and request silence and endure hard work, which is enough to cultivate their personality. I said to Master Wan, "If the Burmese had 100,000 soldiers, the British would not dare to control them." He replied, "Monks are even harder to control because there are no rules to restrain them." Even so, in a national era, it is difficult to win without clear hierarchy. In short, the mixture of religion and education in Burma resembles the scholastic education of the West in the twelfth and thirteenth centuries and the Terakoya education of Japan before the Meiji Restoration. Some parts may be adopted for use in a Datong world that is separated from the government. On the 12th, I lectured at the Overseas Chinese School on the true value of knowledge. This topic was extracted from the first chapter of Kropotkin's "Mutual Aid." Kropotkin opposes the entire world of intellectuals, and all great philosophers such as Kant, Comte, and Spencer were overthrown by him because they could not directly solve the science of human society. The most urgent thing now is to solve society, and we do not have time for religion and metaphysics. The result of advocating war and class struggle is that people kill people, which is no better than cattle and dogs without knowledge. Therefore, people should use proper knowledge to seek solutions to avoid strife and killing, which is true knowledge. Otherwise, knowledge is only knowledge of killing and suicide. All intellectuals should repent early and seek true knowledge. True knowledge is to reach the realm of supreme good Datong without mutual killing. Tong Liu was running a poor people's school there and invited me to visit and observe the Qiankun School in Huangshuitian. They drew water from their own wells, which was very good. They have been running the school for more than ten years. They were former Christians. And influencing all of Europe.

Domestic researchers of Western art do not hesitate to travel long distances to Europe to study, which is an appropriate action for scholars. However, some people tell jokes, "If a dog goes to Europe and runs around for a few years, it will probably still just be a dog." Although this is too harsh, there is deep meaning in it. Because no matter what subject you study, if you do not understand the method of research, you will not gain much. If you blindly follow or chase trends to gain the title of a European student or a PhD, then the meaning of what you study will be very poor. Also, if a generation of art researchers goes to Europe because they admire the scenery or are fascinated by the material civilization, and the result is that they only bring back some Western landscapes and pictures of magnificent architecture, there is not much value in their personal research. And how can they meet the expectations of their domestic comrades? I think that studying the evolution of Western art with a diligent and quiet attitude and a historical perspective is the most important thing for going to Europe to study art. My old friend Wang Yachen has been studying Western painting for more than ten years. In order to make a thorough effort, he went to Europe with his wife, Ms. Rong Junli, in the spring of the seventeenth year. Recently, he returned to China with his works, including 49 copies of representative European paintings from the Renaissance to modern times. Most of the pictures are the same size as the originals. He put almost all of his energy into it for two years. As for his own creations, they were all quick sketches made in a short time, just to leave a mark of his stay in Europe. Many of my friends have gone to Europe to study art, and there are many who have brought back copies of famous European paintings, but few have focused on the two major eras of Western art and engaged in systematic research. In just two years, he has achieved so much and made such a great contribution to domestic researchers of Western art. I would not say that there will be no one like him in the future, but I dare to say that there has been no one like him before. I am just writing down my thoughts, and I cannot avoid offending people. If you say I am flattering, that is not what I am doing.

New Medical Words by Yu Puzhai 162

Seek Ai when sick, this is an ancient teaching. I have always been weak, and after marriage, I took on heavy family responsibilities, which gradually led to overwork and illness. At first, I only thought it was a common flu, but then the cough became frequent, and I also had night sweats and coughing up blood. This was undoubtedly pulmonary tuberculosis without waiting for a doctor's diagnosis. For two and a half years, I spent a lot of money on medicine, but it was not effective, and I tried many miraculous prescriptions and secret remedies. There are many fake medicines in the world. Although newspapers often reveal them, they are often just advertisements. I was only suffering from a long-term illness and was often moved by what I saw. I still remember that the Shenbao published a small talk on medicine by Mr. Zhang on December 12th, which described his experience. I had similar feelings. Thanks to the Yijin Grass issued by the Peisheng Pharmaceutical Company at No. 203 Zhonghua Road, Shanghai, I was cured. It was said that this grass had been tested by the Central Health Testing Institute and certified by the famous doctor Bu Linwu, which made it more reliable. I still held on to my preconceived notions and did not try it. Then I went to ask the old doctor Ding Fubao about the seven of its aspects, and then I bought it and took it. As Mr. Zhang said, I was cured immediately. Now, suddenly, a year has passed. Recently, I heard that the herb has been certified by Dr. Ye Boyang of Baolong Hospital, which shows its miraculous effect and further convinces me that my recovery was not accidental. Therefore, I am writing this new medical commentary to record my happiness.
