Art World

Zhou Xushan on Jiangwan Road 179

After viewing the Shanghai Art Academy's daytime exhibition, because of sitting on tatami mats, it affects the racial heredity. The short-legged, wide-bodied Japanese troops make us feel both comical and surprised. The neat uniforms reflect loyal, stingy faces. No matter how they walk, they can't quite shake off the swaggering gait of Western European soldiers. It can be said that they still retain the original form of dragging wooden clogs, walking with their feet turned inward in a difficult manner. On sunny days, they practice bull-like fighting techniques on the field. The sound of bayonet thrusts is like a wounded female leopard, terrifying and fierce. On rainy days, they practice this combat in their large houses, truly admiring their enthusiastic training, which almost never ceases. They can also skillfully use artillery tactics and foot-powered machine gun carts, speeding across the Jiangwan Road near the shooting range.

In Russia, which sparked a social revolution during the World War, White Russian youths who failed and fled to Shanghai have nothing to do. They are hired as military personnel, wearing yellow uniforms and carrying short guns, and are often transported by trucks to the shooting range to practice shooting. In their deep-set, yellowish-blue eyes, almost everyone emits the fierce intent of alcohol. Although they also train hard in a serious, disciplined, militarized manner, their interpersonal connections seem to have lost their center, thus appearing somewhat like they are just going through the motions with the firearms for the sake of bread. They squander their lives residing in China with decadent exile and enjoyment.

From dawn to dusk every day, the sound of rifles and machine guns from the shooting range continuously assaults our eardrums. They, the Japanese soldiers, White Russian soldiers, British and American soldiers, and soldiers from France and Italy, are all practicing, seemingly taking their assigned missions very seriously, pushing them to the extreme. We know that this is the model produced by Darwinism since the 19th century, becoming the national oppressor of our country, the oppressor of other nations. To put it bluntly, it is the weapon of those who have invaded the weak for the past eighty years.

Our nation, historically known for its great assimilative power, is helpless. This is very obvious. A nation without progress in natural sciences naturally has no possibility of assimilating others. Apart from resorting to integrity to call for large-scale resistance movements, on the one hand, and being assimilated by others, on the other hand, there is almost no other way to think of it. The white and red blood of the past few decades are the expressions of sorrow of our nation's intellectual exhaustion, depleted strength, and erratic behavior. Recently, the imposing manner on the shooting range has affected the eyes and ears of passersby.

Now our nation has awakened in many ways, of course, due to being stimulated too deeply, and we cannot help but raise up. In Shanghai, our national cultural movement is also particularly concentrated on Jiangwan Road.

The national cultural movement on Jiangwan Road is multifaceted, such as social, natural scientific, political, and even artistic and literary, all very active. Among them, the paintbrush is what we often admire and pay attention to. The color and the sound of guns of Darwinism almost occupy the area of the shooting range and Jiangwan Road. The sound of guns has been mentioned earlier; the paintbrush is what I want to talk about now.

In fact, paintbrushes are not commonly seen on Jiangwan Road, but some people holding paintbrushes are seen walking on the road. We have not seen the effects of people holding paintbrushes in ordinary times. It is not like the guns at the shooting range, which seem to be making a great noise.

Today, I strolled into the Shanghai Art Academy's exhibition of student works. The sound of guns from the shooting range was firing continuous tunes. Beforehand, I also encountered a large number of artillery vehicles, all driven by Japanese soldiers, seemingly patrolling around Jiangwan Road with a purpose. I spent an hour amidst the sound of target practice, completing my viewing of the paintings. After leaving the exhibition hall, I had an unforgettable impression in my mind. This unforgettable impression is roughly of two types, but I cannot judge for myself whether these two types of impressions are reasonable. It is just an expression of the heart's jumping in response to the scene.

Now let me write down these two types of impressions lingering in my mind in separate points.

The first type belongs to the objects under the paintbrush; this includes three kinds:

(A) Purely aesthetic, somewhat with hedonistic interest.

(B) Naturalistic (such as still life, landscapes, etc.), with a style of imitation.

(C) The national soul squeezed out by Darwinism.

Regarding type A objects, based on the overall ratio of exhibits in the exhibition, they account for about one-fourth of the total, such as the works of Chen Baoyi, Ms. Guan Zilan, Japanese Mr. Hase Kosho, Man.

Page 22

Gusisiro and Mr. Wang Daoyuan are mostly of this type. The works of some students are also often buried in this category.

Regarding type B objects, they account for approximately two-thirds of the total output, mainly consisting of Ni Yide, Japanese Mr. Nakagawa Kigen, Mei Yuan Long Saburo, and most students' imitations of the willows and catkins along the West Lake.

Regarding type C objects, they are the fewest among the exhibits, mainly consisting of Zhu Yingpeng, and a small number of similar works by Yang Qiuren and Zeng Zhiliang.

The second type belongs to the social experience under the paintbrush; this can also be divided into three types:

(D) Engaged in the world and with rich social observation.

(E) Immersed in sweet dreams and with considerable innocence.

(F) Neither worldly nor unworldly, but having lost the emotions of childhood.

Regarding type D social experience, Wang Daoyuan, Zhu Yingpeng, and Japanese Mr. Akita Yoshiichi are the most abundant, thus creating a feeling of mutual understanding and secluded paths leading to the depths, enabling viewers to obtain a powerful response amidst the sound of guns surrounding the shooting range.

Regarding type E, Ni Yide and Chen Baoyi are the most abundant. From the viewer's perspective, the two authors seem to be proponents of art for art's sake, regardless of whether it is art for life or art for art's sake. In short, social experience is indispensable. To put it bluntly, we cannot leave society. Mr. Ni is a writer and someone I admire and respect the most. Because my hopes are too high, I unconsciously speak excessively. I think Mr. Ni would not consider my words to be obscene exaggeration. Finally, I offer him the phrase "walking from the ivory tower to the crossroads."

Regarding type F, Ms. Guan Zilan's paintings are abundant.

Just as I was writing the manuscript, the sound of night target practice from the shooting range rose sharply, as if telling me to put down my pen. Miscellaneous literary talk.

Ruskin's Peculiarity 180

Ruskin's favorite books in his childhood were the Psalms of the Old Testament and Byron's "Childe Harold." His mother, rich in religious sentiment, was often very enthusiastic about his love of Byron's works.

But Ruskin naturally wouldn't become the kind of man in "Childe Harold." He loved nature, although he was born in the bustling center of London and spent his life there. He was still a singer of nature. Looking at the always azure sky from the beautiful rooftop of the Guvar's house, Ruskin had infinite poetic aspirations for it. His unparalleled work "Modern Painters" can also be said to have arisen from this keen sense of loving nature.

He had a strange aversion to railroads.

"Traveling by rail is not traveling; it's just shipping goods."

He felt this way from the bottom of his heart, believing that the presence of railroads would reduce the beautiful influence of nature on people's minds.

Seeing today's web-like railways, one wonders how Ruskin would sigh. Living in modern times, we can only give him a desolate smile in response to his quirk.

Fortunately, he passed away from this world in 1899. (Su)

Recently, the weather has gradually turned cold, and water heaters are burned in each room day and night to keep guests warm, so business is very prosperous.

Qingfeng Garden

A Trip to Zhenjiang by Wang Chengzi 182

At nine o'clock in the evening, our biology department students on the third floor of the Zibin Courtyard were walking around, talking, laughing, and breaking through the cold, silent, and cool air of this night. At this time, luggage was ready and waiting to depart for a trip to Zhenjiang. After about half an hour, sitting in the car, our hearts had already flown to our destination with the speed of lightning. Everything in front of us was blurred. Arriving at the North Railway Station and getting on the train, although it was still early before the train departed, the crowd was surging and extremely crowded. It was only with great difficulty that we grabbed a space in the back to arrange our positions.

Inside, the students were feeling a little uneasy in the bad air and dense fog of cigarettes.

During the train ride, amidst the fatigue and boredom, we found some laughter to invigorate our spirits. Mr. Chen was the most talkative among the students. He said everything, and if he had something to say, he would say it. If he had nothing to say, he would find an opportunity to say something. It just so happened that an old gentleman sitting next to him was from the same hometown. As soon as they met, they merged like water and milk, opening their talkative boxes.

"I am also from Ningbo," the old gentleman said.

"Yes, we are all from the same hometown," Mr. Chen also said.

"Who are the members of your family?" he asked.

"Parents, brother..." Mr. Chen replied.

"..."

"Ah, I know your brother very well, he is my friend." I only heard this sentence from their conversation.

"What school do you study at and where are you traveling to?" he asked again.

"We are Fudan Biology Department students traveling to Zhenjiang," Mr. Chen replied.

"Are there male and female students in your school? How many female students are there?" He turned his eyes and asked them like that.

"There are more than one hundred female students in total," Mr. Chen replied. Their conversation then turned again.

"When people go out, they rely entirely on friends. Like us, everyone is a friend."

"Speaking is also very important. When you go to a place, you must be able to speak the language of that place. Like Chiang Kai-shek, when he gave speeches in Guangdong, he spoke Cantonese, when he was in the south, he spoke Mandarin, and when he returned to his hometown, he spoke the local dialect."

Their expressions were truly amusing, and their voices were especially loud, causing us all to stare and laugh foolishly. But they didn't feel it at all and were still talking endlessly.

(Taken by Bing) in the female dormitory of Jinan University.

Mr. Lu, who studied abnormal psychology, said, "These two people might have some kind of psychological abnormality."

"Talking too much is also a kind of disease," Mr. Xu also said.

"These two lunatics are simply a natural match, made for each other," Mr. Wang added.

"Hahaha," we couldn't help but burst into laughter when we talked about this matter.

It was late at night, and fatigue urged us into the dreamland we were yearning for.

···········

We all woke up in the faint light of dawn. Mr. Chen could be said to have slept the most comfortably last night because he slept on the luggage rack. Second was Mr. Wang. It was a pity that they really didn't get any sleep all night.

"It's almost seven o'clock now, but we've only passed XX," Mr. Wang said anxiously after looking at his watch.

"Taking a rickshaw would be faster than this," Mr. Lu also frowned and said.

"I heard that the train derailed the day before yesterday, so today it's especially fast and changed to especially slow," a guest said.

Looking at the trees outside the window, they all seemed to be shaking listlessly, making the train seem even slower.

·······

At more than nine o'clock, we finally reached our destination. We sat on rickshaws and walked through the streets, like a long snake, attracting passersby to stare with strange eyes. After about a meal's worth of time, we arrived at the Yipinxiang Hotel. At this time, we were hungry, so after a little grooming, we left the hotel alley and walked into a Wanhualou restaurant. We surrounded a round table. First, three large basins of Zhenjiang's famous dish, stewed pork, were brought over. The flavor of this foreign land was truly delicious. In a short while, it was all eaten up.

Mr. Xu sat high in the seat of honor, his face like a Lohan and his body like a tumbler, showing the appearance of a northerner. He kept shouting, "Hurry up and bring the steamed buns and sesame cakes."

"Mr. Xu, you're rushing your second life again."

Mr. Wang said to him. This was a story from before when they went to Mogan Mountain. Mr. Xu once said that calling for steamed buns and sesame cakes was his second life.

"Mr. Lu sweats the most when he eats," a student said.

"Old Lu, why didn't you bring that big towel?" Mr. Wang asked jokingly.

"I lost it last year when I was swimming in Hangzhou," he replied with a chuckle.

We finished eating the refreshments in conversation and laughter. Mr. Xu no longer needed his second life. Old Lu's face was glowing with sweat and his stomach was patting loudly.

Returning to the hotel, because of the sleepless night, everyone went to their rooms to rest.

In the afternoon, we visited Jinshan Temple. The solemn palaces and the lined-up statues of gods, the giant eyes, the exposed teeth, and the grotesque faces, would make people nervous. Behind the temple, there is a seven-story pagoda. We climbed up the steps and reached the highest level, overlooking the earth as if it were in our grasp. Looking into the distance, Jiao Mountain stood tall in the river, with small boats coming and going in between. At this time, a gentle breeze came, intoxicating people, and unconsciously, our minds were broadened and we had the will to go far and high. We also imitated Confucius and Laozi's tone and recited in a low voice, "Climbing the Jinshan Temple Pagoda and belittling Zhenjiang." Next to the tower, there is a stone pavilion with an inscription that reads "A Panoramic View of the Rivers and Mountains." We took a photo here.

Leaving the temple and turning towards the First Spring Under Heaven, the ancient trees along the road are intertwined and connected into a path. The gentle breeze blows, welcoming people with smiles. Across the bank of the stream, an old fisherman sits leisurely, fishing. This beautiful nature!

Page 30

Ah! The picturesque scenery! You have now cleansed my mind. You will make me forget the troubles of the world and be intoxicated and enjoy being in your embrace.

The fun was not yet over, so we went to Zhenjiang Park. Jiang and Wang, the two of them, are truly admirable. They didn't sleep all night yesterday and still had the courage to run to a distant mountain pavilion to rest. My legs were already a little sore and numb, but they didn't feel tired at all. It was already dusk when we returned to the hotel.

During dinner, the conversation and laughter began again. Mr. Xu, nonsensically, imitated the Shanghai dialect, saying, "This sesame cake is delicious, laixi."

"This bowl of rice is skewed and sweet, lie." He said again with a smile.

"This thing is extremely delicious, jiaoguan youwei," Mr. Wang also followed suit.

"Ah Wang, are we speaking correctly?" She is an old Shanghainese and was asking her for advice.

"You have a few copper coins, have no taste, luo? Meidewei, luo?" Hu also imitated the Hunan dialect that I and my brother spoke, laughing at her.

"You invited me to dinner, did you kill a chicken or did you kill your family?" I also spoke Hubei dialect, laughing at her.

"·········"

One sentence from you and one sentence from me, we finished a meal and our stomachs were full of laughter.

The fatigue from the car ride and the tiredness after sightseeing, not long after dinner, we all drifted off to sleep.

··········

We got up very early the next morning. After a night of sound sleep, our spirits had all returned to their original state. So we bought a boat for a trip to Jiao Mountain. The boat swayed in the middle of the stream, and our spirits also increased. Some stood on the deck, raising their heads to the sky, silently chanting with the sound of the water flowing. Some sat quietly, basking in the sun. Some were browsing the scenery on the river bank. Some were even taking the opportunity to sing. Mr. Xu was singing a Henan folk song. Mr. Huang was playing a Japanese hand harp and singing "Sparrow and Child." Hu also seemed to be sitting at the entrance of the cabin, singing English love songs in a low voice. Mr. Lu also raised his voice and sang his Yixing Beijing opera. Old Wang was even more generous and performed several foxtrots. At this time, we were all indulging in the mountains and rivers. Arriving at Jiao Mountain, we abandoned the boat and landed. Entering Jiao Mountain Temple, several students ran to the main hall to ask for a divination stick. Old Huang said that he was the most unhappy. Both times, it was "down, down." He took off his hat and asked for another divination stick, which was the most auspicious. This way, the gods were also good at flattering. Leaving the temple gate and entering the mountain road, we rested for a while in the pavilion and then went up the towering cliff, following the small path to reach the top of the mountain. With the white sun overhead and the great river flowing eastward, everyone had an indescribable sense of greatness and comfort in their hearts. After lingering for a long time, we returned to the boat by the original route and visited Ganlu Temple again. Troops were stationed in the temple, the buildings were dilapidated, and the scenery was bleak, only for tourists to look back on.

Returning to the hotel, it was not yet four o'clock. With nothing to do, we all read the newspaper to pass the time.

After eating dinner, two or three students each went out to see the lively streets, stroll through the amusement park, buy Zhenjiang specialties, and take a walk in the park. Only Jiang, her nose was pink like a peach, as if she had caught a cold and was afraid of catching a chill, stayed alone in the hotel and did not go out.

At ten o'clock in the evening, we all returned and gathered in a room to discuss many issues regarding hiring more teachers, adding courses, and collecting specimens before going to bed.

On the morning of the third day, we visited Zhenjiang Provincial Middle School. In the reception room, we met a Fudan graduate who was teaching there. Meeting in a foreign land, he was especially courteous in his hospitality, leading us to visit the magnificent dormitories, the clean classrooms, and the complete equipment, all of which demonstrated the spirit of running the school. Walking to the dining hall, he told us that this was a student-run food cooperative. Walking to the back garden, he said,

These trees were planted by students, and this rockery was arranged by students. He also said that because the school is located near Ganlu Temple and built against the city, the terrain is extremely high, overlooking the scenery as if it were under the table. Therefore, the school would like to open up a park in the open space behind the school so that students can visit, look out, and rest during their free time, so as to get some physical and mental cultivation. Finally, he took two photos for us, and we were treated to tea and refreshments, exchanged greetings, and agreed to meet again before saying goodbye and leaving the school.

Leaving Zhenjiang Middle School, some of us went straight to the train station, and some returned to the hotel to pack our luggage. At about three o'clock in the afternoon, we boarded the train and shouted "Returning home!"
